Scope of Authority in Agency for Litigation and Possession
Rulings on agency in litigation and possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether an agent for litigation has authority to take possession, and distinguish between debt and specific property.

Core Idea
An agent for litigation does not automatically have authority to take possession of a specific item, but taking possession of a debt implies authority to litigate.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh manual clarifies the precise scope of an agent's authority in legal disputes. A common point of confusion is whether an agent appointed to represent in court can also take possession of the property after winning. The text distinguishes between two types of property: debts (dayn) and specific items (ayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of agency discussed
The passage discusses agency for litigation (khusumat) and agency for taking possession (qabd). Note the property type: ayn (specific item) vs. dayn (debt).
2
Note the ruling for each combination
An agent for litigation is automatically an agent for taking possession of a debt? No, the text says agent for qabd of dayn is agent for khusumat (per Abu Hanifa), but agent for khusumat is not agent for qabd of ayn. Also, agent for qabd of ayn is not agent for khusumat.
The reverse is not stated: agent for khusumat is not agent for qabd of ayn.
3
Apply to divorce and manumission
The same distinction applies: an agent authorized to perform divorce or manumission is not automatically authorized for the other without specific grant.
4
Understand the scenario of two agents
If two agents are appointed for litigation, both must jointly take possession of a debt. One cannot act alone.
5
Recognize the effect of the agent's admission in court
If an agent for litigation makes an admission (iqrar) before a judge concerning the principal, the admission is binding on the principal unless the principal explicitly excluded such admissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض
وکیل بالخصومت وکیل بالقبض ہے یا نہیں
خصومت کے دو وکیل ہوں تو قرضہ پر دونوں ایک ساتھ قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں
امام ابو حنیفہ کے نقطہ نظر میں قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل خصومت کا بھی وکیل ہے
عین پر قبضہ کا وکیل خصومت کا وکیل نہیں
مذکورہ بالا حکم طلاق اور عناق کا بھی ہے
کیل بالخصومت نے قاضی کے پاس اپنے مؤکل پر کچھ اقرار کیا تو وکیل کا اقرار مؤکل پر جائز ہوگا موکل نے اقرار کا استثناء کیا تو یہ استثناء درست ہے یا نہیں
ایک شخص دوسرے کی جانب سے مال کا کفیل ہو گیا پھر صاحب مال نے کفیل کو مدیون سے مال پر قبضہ کرنے کا
وکیل بنا یا وکیل بنے گا یا نہیں
کسی شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ میں فلاں غائب کی طرف سے اس کا قرضہ وصول کرنے کا وکیل ہوں قرضدار نے اس
کی تصدیق کی تو قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ قرضہ وکیل کے سپر د کرے
اگر قرضدار مال دیتے وقت وکیل کو ضامن بنا دے
Chapter on Agency in Litigation and Taking Possession: Is an agent for litigation also an agent for taking possession? If there are two agents for litigation, they both can take possession of a debt together. In Imam Abu Hanifa's view, an agent for taking possession of a debt is also an agent for litigation. An agent for taking possession of a specific thing is not an agent for litigation. The same ruling applies to divorce and manumission. If an agent for litigation makes an admission before a judge concerning his principal, that admission is valid against the principal. If the principal excludes the admission, is that exclusion valid? A person became a guarantor for property on behalf of another; then the owner of the property made the guarantor an agent to take possession of the property from the debtor. Will he become an agent? A person claimed: 'I am an agent to collect a debt on behalf of so-and-so who is absent.' The debtor confirmed this; then the debtor will be ordered to hand over the debt to the agent. If the debtor, when handing over the property, makes the agent a guarantor...
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This chapter deals with agency in litigation (wakalah bil khusumah) and taking possession (qabd). The key issue is whether an agent appointed to litigate on behalf of the principal also has authority to take possession of the property after winning. According to the text, an agent for litigation does not automatically have authority to take possession of a specific item (ayn), but an agent for taking possession of a debt (dayn) is also considered an agent for litigation according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If there are two agents for litigation, both must jointly take possession of a debt. The same rule applies to divorce and manumission (the agent must be specifically authorized). If the agent for litigation makes an admission in court, it binds the principal unless the principal explicitly excluded such admissions. If a surety (kafil) is then appointed as agent to collect the debt, he becomes an agent. If a person claims to be an agent for an absent creditor and the debtor confirms, the debtor must pay the agent. However, if the debtor asks the agent to guarantee the debt, that requires separate consideration. These are detailed rulings from Hanafi fiqh on the scope of agency in legal proceedings.

Key Terms
خصومت (khusumat): Litigation or legal dispute; agency to represent in court.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person is appointed as an agent to take possession of a specific item (ayn), does he also have authority to litigate?
A) Yes, automatically.
B) No, he does not have authority to litigate.
C) Only if the principal also says so.
D) Only for debts, not for specific items.

Key Takeaway
An agent for litigation does not automatically have authority to take possession of specific property, but an agent for taking possession of a debt is presumed to have litigation authority in the Hanafi school.

Conditions for a Valid Lawsuit
Opening rulings from Kitab al-Da'wa: conditions and procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main conditions for a valid lawsuit in Hanafi fiqh and explain the specific requirement for land claims and the judge's procedure upon acceptance.

Core Idea
A valid lawsuit requires clear subject matter; the defendant must respond, not the plaintiff withdraw.

In Hanafi judiciary (qada), a lawsuit (da'wa) is a claim made in court seeking a right. Not every claim is accepted; specific conditions must be met. This lesson covers the foundational rules: the plaintiff cannot be forced to drop the case, but the defendant can be compelled to respond. For land disputes, the boundaries must be precisely stated. Once the claim is deemed correct, the judge asks the defendant for a response; an admission leads to a ruling against the defendant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The passage discusses the lawsuit (da'wa) itself. Determine what makes it valid or invalid, not the ruling on the underlying right. Here, the act is 'bringing a claim'.
2
Extract the condition about the plaintiff
The text states: 'The plaintiff cannot be compelled to withdraw the lawsuit.' This means the plaintiff has the right to pursue the claim or drop it voluntarily. The court cannot force a withdrawal.
Plaintiff = mudda'i
3
Extract the condition about the defendant
The defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) can be compelled to respond. Unlike the plaintiff, the defendant cannot refuse to participate; he must answer the claim.
4
Identify the special requirement for land claims
For land (zamin), the plaintiff must state the four boundaries (hudud arba'a) to precisely identify the subject matter. Without them, the claim is ambiguous and not acceptable.
This ensures the property is specifically identified.
5
Trace the judge's procedure after a valid claim
Once the lawsuit is deemed correct (sahih), the judge asks the defendant about the claim to clarify the basis of judgment. If the defendant admits (iqrar), the judge immediately rules against him. If he denies, further evidence is needed.
Admission = iqrar; denial leads to evidence from plaintiff.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الدعوى
دعویٰ صحیح ہونے کی شرطیں
مدعی پر ترک دعوی سے خصومت پر جبر نہیں اور مدنی علیہ پر جبر ہے
دعوی کب قبول کیا جائے گا
زمین کے دعوئی کیلئے زمین کی حدود اربعہ بیان کرے
دعوی صحیح ہو جائے تو قاضی مدنی علیہ سے اس کے بارے میں سوال کرے تا کہ جہت حکم کھل جائے اگر مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا تو قاضی مدعی علیہ پر دھونی کا حکم کرے گا
Book of Lawsuit
Conditions for a lawsuit to be correct.
The plaintiff cannot be compelled to withdraw the lawsuit; but the defendant can be compelled.
When will a lawsuit be accepted?
For a land claim, he must state the four boundaries of the land.
If the lawsuit is correct, the judge asks the defendant about it so that the basis of judgment becomes clear. If the defendant acknowledges, the judge will give judgment against the defendant.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This is the beginning of the Book of Lawsuit (Kitab al-Da'wa) and contains foundational principles. First, conditions for a valid lawsuit: The plaintiff (mudda'i) cannot be forced to withdraw his claim; the lawsuit is his right. However, the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) can be compelled to respond and appear in court. This is because the plaintiff is seeking a right, while the defendant may be avoiding his obligation. A lawsuit is accepted only if it meets specific conditions: for land, the plaintiff must specify the boundaries (hudud arba'a) to identify the subject matter precisely. Once a lawsuit is deemed correct, the judge asks the defendant about the claim to clarify the basis for judgment (jihah al-hukm). If the defendant admits (iqrar), the judge issues a ruling against him. This procedural structure ensures the lawsuit is clear, the defendant's response is heard, and the judgment is based on admission or evidence. These are the Hanafi rules for court proceedings.

Key Terms
دعویٰ (da'wa): Lawsuit or claim made in court seeking a right.
مدعی (mudda'i): Plaintiff: one who brings a claim.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayh): Defendant: one against whom the claim is made.
حدود اربعہ (hudud arba'a): The four boundaries of a piece of land, required to be stated in a land claim.
اقرار (iqrar): Admission or acknowledgement of a claim by the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a land claim in a lawsuit?
A) The approximate location.
B) The four boundaries of the land.
C) The name of the previous owner.
D) A written deed.

Key Takeaway
A lawsuit is valid only if the plaintiff is not forced to withdraw, the defendant can be compelled, and for land, the precise four boundaries are stated; then the judge asks the defendant, and admission leads to judgment.

Who Is Not a Proper Litigant: Claims of Absent Ownership
Rules for when defendant claims absent ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for when a defendant's claim of absent ownership repels litigation, and identify whether evidence (bayyinah) is required for each.

Core Idea
A defendant who proves with witnesses that property belongs to an absent person becomes a non-litigant.

In litigation, the defendant cannot simply claim the property belongs to someone else to avoid the case. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents three scenarios: when the defendant claims the item is a deposit or pledge from an absent person, when he claims he bought it from an absent seller, and when the claimant admits he bought it from the same person the defendant claims deposited it. The rulings differ based on whether the defendant provides evidence and the nature of the claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage gives three distinct cases: (1) Defendant claims the items are a deposit (wadi'ah) or pledge (rahn) from an absent person. (2) Defendant claims he bought a slave from an absent person. (3) Claimant says the item is stolen or he bought it, and the possessor says it is a deposit from an absent person (with or without evidence). List them clearly.
The text uses 'مدعلی علیہ' for defendant, and the scenarios are intermixed.
2
Determine the effect on litigation for each
For scenario 1: If the defendant provides witnesses that the item is a deposit/pledge from an absent person, litigation is not repelled? Actually the passage poses a question. For scenario 2: The absent person becomes the proper defendant. For scenario 3: If the claimant says it is stolen and the possessor proves deposit, litigation is NOT repelled; but if the claimant says he bought it and the possessor claims deposit from the same seller, litigation is dismissed without evidence.
The rulings are nuanced; note the difference between 'خصومت دفع نہ ہوگی' (litigation not repelled) and 'خصومت ساقط ہو جائے گی' (litigation dismissed).
3
Note the role of evidence
In scenario 1, the defendant must produce witnesses for his claim to affect litigation. In scenario 2, no evidence is mentioned; the absent seller becomes the defendant. In scenario 3, evidence is crucial: if the claimant alleges theft and the possessor produces evidence of deposit, litigation continues; but if the claimant admits buying from the same person, the defendant's claim of deposit is accepted without evidence.
Evidence (بینہ) shifts the procedural burden.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The phrase 'بعض نے کہا' (some said) indicates a difference of opinion. Identify what is disputed: likely whether the defendant's claim of deposit without evidence is accepted when the claimant admits buying from the same person, or whether evidence is always required.
This ikhtilaf is among Hanafi scholars; the relied-upon position may require evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيمن لا يكون خصما
مدعلی علیہ نے کہا کہ یہ چیزیں فلاں غائب نے میرے پاس ودیعت یا بطور رہن رکھی ہیں یا میں نے انہیں نصب کیا ہے، اور اس پر اس نے گواہ بھی قائم کر دیئے تو اس کے بعد مدعی اور اس کے درمیان خصومت قائم ہوگی یا نہیں۔ مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ میں نے اس غلام کو فلاں غائب سے خریدا ہے وہ شخصم ہو گا مدعی نے کہا کہ یہ چیز میری چوری ہوئی ہے قابض نے کہا کہ فلاں نے میرے پاس ودیعت رکھا ہے اور بعینہ قائم کر دئیے تو خصومت دفع نہ ہوگی مدعی نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز فلاں سے خریدی ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ اس نے یہ چیز میرے پاس ودیعت رکھی ہے تو خصومت بغیر بینہ کے ساقط ہو جائے گی
Section on who is not a litigant.
The defendant said: 'These items are a deposit (wadi'ah) or pledge (rahn) with me from so-and-so who is absent, or I have [nusba?] them,' and he also produced witnesses on that; then after that, will litigation exist between the claimant and him or not? (First case) The defendant said: 'I bought this slave from so-and-so who is absent; that person is the [seller].' (Second case) The claimant said: 'This item is stolen from me.' The possessor said: 'So-and-so deposited (wadi'ah) it with me,' and he produced evidence; then litigation will not be repelled. (Third case) The claimant said: 'I bought this item from so-and-so' and some said: 'He deposited this item with me,' then litigation will be dismissed without evidence?
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This section (fasl) deals with situations where the defendant claims that the disputed property does not belong to him but to an absent third party. If the defendant provides witnesses that the property is a deposit (wadi'ah) or pledge (rahn) from an absent person, or that he has it as collateral (nusba?), then the question is whether the claimant can continue litigation against the defendant. The text gives several case scenarios: if the defendant claims to have purchased the slave from an absent person, then the absent person is considered the seller, so litigation may be with that absent person. If the claimant says the item is stolen and the possessor says it is a deposit from someone else and provides evidence, then litigation is not repelled (i.e., the claimant can still proceed). If the claimant says he bought it from someone and the possessor says it is a deposit from that same someone, then litigation is dismissed without evidence (meaning the defendant's statement without evidence is accepted). The rulings depend on whether the defendant's relationship to the absent person is credible.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; an item left for safekeeping with another.
خصم (khasm): Litigant; a party to a legal dispute.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence; typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the defendant claims he purchased a slave from an absent person, what is the effect on the current litigation?
A) The litigation is dismissed immediately.
B) The absent person becomes the proper defendant.
C) The defendant must produce the slave.
D) The case is postponed until the absent person is found.

Key Takeaway
A defendant who proves by witnesses that the disputed property belongs to an absent person is not a proper litigant; absent evidence, the claim alone does not repel litigation.

When a Defendant Claims Property Belongs to an Absent Person
Rulings on when a defendant's claim of absent ownership prevents litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether litigation continues when a defendant claims the disputed property belongs to an absent person and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A defendant's claim of absent ownership does not automatically dismiss the case; evidence and claim nature matter.

This lesson dissects a passage from a Hanafi text on judicial procedure (qada). The core question: if a defendant claims that the property in dispute belongs to an absent third party (e.g., as deposit or pledge), does the court dismiss the case? The answer depends on the type of claim and the evidence provided, and there is a known intra-Hanafi difference on the requirement for dismissal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defendant's claims
Read the passage and list the types of claims the defendant makes: deposit, pledge, purchase, or installation. The claimant also makes counterclaims (theft, purchase).
Each claim type may affect the ruling differently.
2
Determine the effect of witnesses
The passage asks what happens if the defendant brings witnesses (‘alaihi qaim kar diye’). The text indicates that in some cases the litigation continues, in others it is dropped.
The Arabic phrase ‘ba'aynihi qaim kar diye’ means the defendant established exactly what he claimed.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The phrase ‘ba‘z ne kaha’ (some said) signals a disagreement. Some Hanafi scholars hold that if the defendant claims a deposit from an absent person and brings witnesses, the suit is dropped. Others (the relied-upon view) require that the defendant prove the property is not his own.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the litigation is not dismissed unless the defendant provides clear evidence that the property belongs to the absent person and that the defendant has no ownership claim.
This protects the claimant's right to pursue ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيمن لا يكون خصما مدعلی علیہ نے کہا کہ یہ چیزیں فلاں غائب نے میرے پاس ودیعت یا بطور رہن رکھی ہیں یا میں نے انہیں نصب کیا ہے ، اور اس پر اس نے گواہ بھی قائم کر دیئے تو اس کے بعد مدعی اور اس کے درمیان خصومت قائم ہوگی یا نہیں مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ میں نے اس غلام کو فلاں غائب سے خریدا ہے وہ شخصم ہو گا مدعی نے کہا کہ یہ چیز میری چوری ہوئی ہے قابض نے کہا کہ فلاں نے میرے پاس ودیعت رکھا ہے اور بعینہ قائم کر دیئے تو خصومت دفع نہ ہوگی مدعی نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز فلاں سے خریدی ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ اس نے یہ چیز میرے پاس ودیعت رکھی سےتو خصومت بغیر ہینہ کے ساقط ہو جائے گی
Section on who is not a litigant. The defendant said: 'These items are placed with me as a deposit or pledge by so-and-so absent, or I have installed them,' and upon that he also produced witnesses, then after that will litigation be established between the claimant and him? The defendant said: 'I bought this slave from so-and-so absent, he is the person.' The claimant said: 'This item was stolen from me.' The possessor said: 'So-and-so placed it with me as a deposit' and he established exactly that, then litigation is not repelled. The claimant said: 'I bought this item from so-and-so,' and some said: 'He placed this item with me as a deposit,' then litigation is dropped without evidence.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This is a parsing exercise from a Hanafi fiqh text, likely from a chapter on litigation (qada). The author presents various scenarios where a defendant claims that the disputed property belongs to an absent person (gha'ib). The text asks whether the litigation proceeds or is dismissed after the defendant brings witnesses. If the defendant claims the item is a deposit or pledge from an absent person and provides witnesses, the litigation may continue. If the defendant claims he bought the slave from an absent person, the litigation situation is different. If the plaintiff claims theft and the possessor claims deposit with witnesses, the litigation is not repelled. However, if the plaintiff claims purchase and some say the defendant claimed deposit, the litigation is dropped without evidence (bina). The text mentions 'بعض نے کہا' (some said), indicating intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars hold that in certain claims, the suit is dismissed if the defendant's claim is plausible, while others require evidence. The relied-upon position likely requires evidence to dismiss the case.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): Litigant or opponent in a lawsuit
ودیعت (wadi'at): Deposit; property entrusted to another for safekeeping
رہن (rahn): Pledge; property given as security for a debt
خصومت (khusumat): Litigation or court dispute between parties
بعینہ (bi'aynihi): Exactly as stated; precisely the same thing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the defendant claims the item is a deposit from an absent person and brings witnesses, what happens to the litigation?
A) The litigation is automatically dismissed
B) The litigation continues because the claim is not established
C) The litigation is dismissed only if the witnesses are from the absent person
D) The litigation is put on hold until the absent person returns

Key Takeaway
The defendant's claim of absent ownership requires credible evidence of non-ownership; the litigation is not automatically dismissed.

Retraction from Testimony on Excessive Mehr
Ruling on witnesses' liability for excess dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses' liability when they retract testimony regarding an excessive dower and explain the reasoning based on compensated vs. uncompensated loss.

Core Idea
Witnesses guarantee only the excess dower—loss compensated by marital rights does not incur liability.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shahadat: when witnesses testify to a dower higher than the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) and then retract, what are they liable for? The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between the portion of the dower that is compensated by marital rights (milk al-bud') and the excess, which is uncompensated. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principle that loss with consideration does not create liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage to understand the facts: a woman claims dower exceeding mahr al-mithl, witnesses testify accordingly, then retract. The ruling: marriage stands, but witnesses guarantee only the excess.
The marriage is not rescinded because the dower obligation is valid; only the testimony caused extra loss.
2
Distinguish between compensated and uncompensated loss
The proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is compensated because the husband receives marital rights (milk al-bud') in exchange. This is itlaf bi al-iwad, which does not trigger guarantee. The excess is itlaf bila iwad, which does trigger guarantee.
Compensation (iwad) is key to negating liability.
3
Apply the principle to the witnesses' liability
Since the excess was caused without any benefit to the husband, the witnesses must make good that loss. They are liable for the excess amount only.
The liability is limited to the amount above mahr al-mithl.
4
Understand the rational (istihsan) basis
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than strict qiyas. The authority is Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
Istihsan allows departure from strict analogy to achieve equitable outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
وان شهدا باكثر من مهر المثل ثم رجعا ضمنا الزيادة لانهما اتلفاها من غير عوض
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے کسی مرد پر مہر مثل سے زائد کے عوض نکاح کا دعوی کیا مثلاً مہر مثل ایک ہزار روپیہ ہیں اور اس نے پندرہ سو روپیہ کے عوض کا دعویٰ کیا اور مرد اس واقعہ کا منکر ہے، پس دو گواہوں نے عورت کے دعوی کے مطابق گواہی دے دی اور قاضی نے فیصلہ کر دیا پھر دونوں گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو نہ یہ نکاح فسخ ہو گا اور نہ یہ دونوں گواہ مہر مثل کی مقدار کا ضامن ہوں گے۔ البتہ مہر مثل سے زائد یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ مہر مثل یعنی ایک ہزار کا اتلاف تو اتلاف بعوض ملک بضع ہے اور اتلاف بالعوض کی صورت میں ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا لہذا مہر مثل کی مقدار کا ضمان گواہوں پر واجب نہ ہوگا مگر چونکہ مہر مثل کی مقدار سے زائد یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کا اتلاف بلا عوض ہے یعنی ان پانچ سو روپیہ کے عوض شوہر کو کچھ نہیں ملا اسلئے ان پانچ سو روپیہ کا ضمان گواہوں پر واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اتلاف بلا عوض ضمان کو واجب کرتا ہے۔
The Book of Retraction from Testimonies. And if they (two witnesses) testified to more than the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) and then retracted, they guarantee the excess because they caused loss of that excess without compensation. Explanation: The issue is that a woman claimed marriage against a man for a dower exceeding the proper dower; e.g., proper dower is one thousand rupees and she claimed one thousand five hundred, and the man denies. So two witnesses testified according to her claim and the judge passed judgment. Then both witnesses retracted their testimony. The marriage is not rescinded, nor are the witnesses liable for the amount of the proper dower. However, they are liable for the excess, i.e., five hundred rupees, because the loss of the proper dower was compensated by the marital right (milk al-bud'), and in a compensated loss, guarantee is not obligatory. But the excess was caused without compensation, so they guarantee it because loss without compensation entails guarantee.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shahadat. It addresses a scenario where witnesses testify to a dower amount exceeding the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) and then retract. The key principle is that loss (itlaf) with consideration (bi 'iwad) does not incur liability, while loss without consideration does. Here, the husband pays the dower in exchange for marital rights (milk al-bud'), so the base dower is considered compensated. However, the excess above the proper dower is not compensated, so witnesses are liable for that excess. The ruling is clear: they guarantee only the additional amount.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower: the amount typically given to a woman of similar status in her family, used as a baseline when no dower is specified or when excess is claimed.
ملک بضع (milk al-bud'): The right of sexual access in marriage, considered a valuable consideration (iwad) for the dower.
اتلاف بالعوض (itlaf bi al-iwad): Loss with compensation: a situation where the loss is offset by receiving something in exchange, which negates liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of witnesses retracting testimony after confirming a dower higher than mahr al-mithl, what amount do they guarantee?
A) The entire dower amount
B) Only the mahr al-mithl
C) Only the excess above mahr al-mithl
D) Nothing, because marriage is valid

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract a false testimony on excessive dower are liable only for the amount above the proper dower, because loss with compensation does not create a guarantee.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Retraction from Testimony on Sale at Below Market Price
Ruling on witnesses' liability in sale testimony retraction via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for witnesses' liability when testifying to a sale below market value and retracting, distinguishing between compensated and uncompensated loss.

Core Idea
Witnesses guarantee the shortfall in sale testimony when loss is uncompensated, even if the seller fails to rescind.

This lesson examines a specific case in qada (judicial testimony): witnesses who testify to a sale at below market price and then retract. Using qiyas from the earlier dower case, the Hanafi school establishes liability for the uncompensated portion. The passage also addresses a nuanced objection involving the seller's option (khiyar al-ba'i).

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios
When witnesses testify to a sale at market value or above, they are not liable because the seller receives full compensation. When below market value, they guarantee the shortfall because that portion is uncompensated loss.
The key distinction is whether the loss is compensated (itlaf bi al-iwad) or uncompensated (itlaf bi la iwad).
2
Identify the underlying principle
Compensated loss does not trigger liability; uncompensated loss does. This is analogous to the dower case where witnesses who testified to excessive mehr and retracted guaranteed the excess above mahr al-mithl.
The principle is derived from the maxim: 'Itlaf bi al-iwad is like no loss.'
3
Analyze the khiyar al-ba'i objection
One might argue that if the sale includes the seller's option (khiyar al-ba'i), the seller's failure to rescind causes the loss, not the witnesses. However, the Hanafi response is that the cause of ownership transfer is the original sale established by testimony; the seller's silence does not break the causal chain.
The ruling is attributed to the original cause (isnad al-hukm ila al-sabab), not the subsequent silence.
4
Apply the qiyas panel
Asl: witnesses testify to mehr above mahr al-mithl and retract → they guarantee the excess (hukm). Far: witnesses testify to sale below market value and retract. Illa: loss without compensation. Hukm far: they guarantee the shortfall.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) with the illa extracted via tanqih al-manat.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that witnesses are liable for the deficiency regardless of whether the sale is final or includes the seller's option. This is the zahir al-riwayah position supported by al-Marghinani.
The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on objective causation.

Source Text

قال وان شهدا ببيع شيء بمثل القيمة او اكثر ثم رجعا لم يضمنا لانه ليس باتلاف معنى نظرا الى العوض وإن كان باقل من القيمة ضمنا النقصان لانهما اتلفا هذا الجزء بلا عوض ولا فرق بين ان يكون البيع باتا او فيه خيار البائع لان السبب هو البيع السابق فيضاف الحكم عند سقوط الخيار اليه فيضاف التلف اليهم
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری مثلاً حامد نے دعویٰ کیا کہ خالد نے اپنا یہ غلام جو ہزار روپیہ قیمت کا ہے ہزار روپیہ کے عوض یا ڈیڑھ ہزار روپیہ کے عوض مجھ کو فروخت کر دیا ہے اور بائع اس کا منکر ہے۔ پس ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور جب اتلاف بالعوض کی صورت میں ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا تو ان گواہوں پر بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر مشتری نے قیمت سے کم کے عوض مثلاً پانچ سو روپیہ کے عوض مذکور غلام خریدنے کا دعوی کیا اور اسی کے مطابق گواہوں نے گواہی دی اور پھر قاضی کے فیصلے کے بعد گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو دونوں گواہ بائع کے واسطے مقدار نقصان یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کے ضامن ہوں گے سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اتلاف بلاعوض کی صورت میں تلف کرنے والے پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا گواہوں پر اس مقدار کا ضمان واجب ہوگا جس کو بلاعوض تلف کیا ہے یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ جو مقدار نقصان ہیں، گواہ ان کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قیمت سے کم کے عوض بیع کی گواہی دینے کی صورت میں گواہ مقدار نقصان کے ضامن ہوں گے، بیع خواہ قطعی اور نافذ ہو خواہ خیار بائع کی وجہ سے موقوف ہو یہ عبارت دراصل ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جب گواہوں نے کم قیمت کے عوض بیع کی گواہی دی جس میں بائع کو خیار شرط حاصل ہے تو گواہوں نے بائع کی کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی ہے کیونکہ گواہوں نے ایسی بیع کی شہادت دی ہے جس میں بائع نے اپنی گواہی سے ثابت کیا ہے۔ لہذا مدت خیار گذر جانے کے بعد سقوط خیار کے وقت مبیع سے بائع کی ملک زائل ہونے کا حکم اسی بیع سابق کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ جس بیع کو گواہی سے ثابت کیا گیا ہے۔ پس جب زوال ملک کا حکم بیع سابق کی طرف منسوب ہے اور بیع سابق گواہوں کی گواہی سے حاصل ہوئی ہے تو اس مبیع کا تلف کرنا گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ اور جب مبیع کا تلف کرنا گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہے تو جس قدر مبیع کا اتلاف بلا عوض ہے اس کا ضمان بھی گواہوں پر واجب ہوگا۔
He said: And if they testify to the sale of something for its equivalent value or more, then retract, they are not liable because it is not considered loss with respect to consideration. But if it is for less than the value, they guarantee the shortfall because they caused loss of that part without compensation. There is no difference whether the sale is final or includes an option for the seller, because the cause is the previous sale, so the ruling, when the option lapses, is attributed to it, and thus the loss is attributed to them. Explanation: The scenario is that the buyer, e.g., Hamid, claimed that Khalid sold him this slave worth one thousand rupees for one thousand or one thousand five hundred rupees, and the seller denies. The buyer produced witnesses and they testified accordingly. After the judge's judgment, the witnesses retracted. They are not liable to the seller because although they caused the loss of the slave, the seller received full compensation, so it is a compensated loss. As previously established, a compensated loss is like no loss, so no liability. But if the buyer claimed purchase for a lower price, e.g., five hundred rupees, and witnesses testified accordingly, then after judgment they retract, they guarantee the shortfall (five hundred rupees) because they caused loss of that portion without compensation. The author of al-Hidayah said that in case of sale below value, witnesses guarantee the shortfall regardless of whether the sale is final or includes the seller's option. This addresses a question: If the sale includes a condition giving the seller the option to rescind, then the seller's ownership does not immediately cease. After the option period (three days) passes silently, the sale becomes binding, and the seller's silence indicates consent. So how can witnesses be liable? The answer: Although the seller could have rescinded, the cause of ownership transfer is the original sale established by their testimony. So at the moment the option lapses, the transfer of ownership is attributed to that sale, and thus the loss is attributed to the witnesses. Therefore, they are liable for the uncompensated portion.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling for witnesses who testify to a sale and then retract. The principle is the same as in the dower case: compensation negates liability. If the sale price equals or exceeds the market value, the seller receives full compensation, so witnesses are not liable. If the price is below market value, they are liable for the shortfall. The commentary addresses a subtle point: even if the sale includes the seller's option to rescind (khiyar al-ba'i), the liability still falls on the witnesses because the ultimate transfer of ownership is caused by the original sale they testified to. The seller's failure to rescind does not absolve the witnesses; rather, the chain of causation goes back to their testimony. This shows the Hanafi commitment to objective causality (isnad al-hukm ila al-sabab).

Key Terms
خیار البائع (khiyar al-ba'i): The seller's option to rescind the sale within a specified period (typically three days), during which ownership does not transfer.
اتلاف بالعوض (itlaf bi al-iwad): Loss compensated by a countervalue, treated as if no loss occurred for liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses testify to a sale at half the market value and the seller had a three-day option to rescind but did not, what is the Hanafi ruling on the witnesses' liability?
A) They are not liable because the seller consented by not rescinding.
B) They are liable for the whole market value because they caused the sale.
C) They are liable for the difference between market value and sale price.
D) They are liable only if the sale was final without any option.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses guarantee the shortfall in sale testimony when the price is below market value, even if the seller had the option to rescind.

Witness Retraction After Qisas: Hanafi Refutation of Shafi'i Analogy
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i's qiyas on witness retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that witnesses who retract after qisas are liable for diyah, not qisas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using analogy to coercion.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract after qisas pay diyah, not qisas – because testimony does not inevitably lead to killing when forgiveness is recommended.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a detailed Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i position on witness liability after retraction. The dispute hinges on whether testimony is equivalent to coercion (ikrah) as a cause of killing. We will explore the Hanafi arguments – from causality, attribution, and doubt (shubha) – to understand why diyah applies instead of qisas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: witnesses who retract after their testimony led to qisas are liable for diyah, not qisas. Note the hukm level (wajib).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds witnesses liable for qisas, analogizing them to a coercer (mukrih) in ikrah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: coercer is liable for qisas because his action leads to killing; similarly, witnesses' testimony leads to qisas, so they should be liable.
This qiyas is based on the idea that both are causative agents.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Break down the three Hanafi counter-arguments: (1) testimony is not necessarily conducive to killing because forgiveness is recommended; (2) attribution of killing is to the guardian, not witnesses; (3) even if witnesses are cause, shubha (doubt) removes qisas but not diyah.
Each argument independently invalidates the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – witnesses pay diyah; Shafi'i – witnesses are subject to qisas. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم
۱۵۹
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
سے روک ہی دیتے ہیں۔ پس جب مکرہ ( مجبور شخص ) کو شرعاً اور عادہ اس قتل سے روکا جاتا ہے تو اکراہ قبل کی طرف زیادہ مفضی نہ ہوگا بہر حال ثابت ہو گیا کہ شہادت سبیت اور مفضی الی القتل ہونے میں اکراہ سے بڑھ کر ہے اور ا کراہ کی صورت میں مکرہ (اکراہ کرنے والا ) جو مسبب ہے اس کو قصاصا بدرجہ اولی قتل کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قتل ، ایک فعل کا نام ہے اور وہ فعل قتل گواہوں کی طرف سے پایا نہیں گیا، بلکہ قاتل کے قتل کا مرتکب ولی قصاص ہے اور ولی قصاص پر قاتل کے قتل کا قصاص لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب ولی قصاص جو مر تکب قتل ہے اس پر قاتل کے قتل کا قصاص لازم نہیں ہوتا تو اسکے علاوہ یعنی گواہ جنہوں نے قاتل کے قتل کا ارتکاب نہیں کیا ہے۔ ان پر قاتل کے قتل کا قصاص کس طرح لازم ہوگا۔
حاصل یہ کہ شہادت سے رجوع کرنے کے بعد گواہوں سے قاتل کے قتل کا قصاص وصول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ وكذا التسبياً الخ سے صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا رد کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ گواہ ، قاتل کے قتل کا مسبب مہیا کرنے والے بھی نہیں ہیں یعنی گواہوں کی گواہی سبب قتل نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ کسی کام کا سبب وہ ہوتا ہے جو غالبا اس کام تک پہنچا دے ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ مفضی الی اشی مشی کا سبب ہوتا ہے اور یہاں گواہوں کی گواہی مفضی الی القتل نہیں ہے یعنی گواہوں کی گواہی کے بعد بھی قاتل کا قتل ضروری نہیں ہے کیوں کہ قاتل کو معاف کرنا مندوب اور مستحب ہے بلکہ ہر معاملہ میں معافی اور درگزر کرنا شریعت کی نظر میں پسندیدہ اور مندوب ہے۔ چنانچہ غیر مدخول بہا مطلقہ کے مہر کے بارے میں باری عزاسمہ کا ارشاد ہے
واَنْ تَعْفُوا أَقْرَبُ للتَّقْوَى (بقره)
مردوں کا معاف کر دینا پر ہیز گاری کے زیادہ قریب ہے
مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد، بیوی کو پورا مہر ادا کر چکا اور دخول سے پہلے طلاق دیدی تو مرد، بیوی سے نصف مہر واپس نہ لے بلکہ عورت
کے پاس پورا مہر چھوڑ دے اور درگزر کرے اور سور دما ئدہ نہیں فرمایا ہے
وَالْجُرُوحَ قِصَاصٌ فَمَنْ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ فَهُوَ كَفَّارَةً لَّهُ
زخموں کا بدلا ان کے برابر ہے پھر جس نے معاف کر دیا تو وہ مجروح گناہ سے پاک ہو گیا
مطلب یہ ہے کہ زخموں کے قصاص کو معاف کر دینا مجروح کے گناہوں کا کفارہ بن جاتا ہے جیسا کہ بعض احادیث میں اس کی تصریح موجود ہے۔ ان دونوں آیات سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ معاف کرنا اور درگزر کرنا شریعت اسلام میں پسندیدہ اور مندوب ہے اور
احادیث میں ہے ،
من كظم غيظاً و هو يقدر على انفاذه ملأ الله قلبه امناً وإيماناً جس نے نفاذ کی قدرت کے باوجود اپنا غصہ فی لیا اللہ تعالیٰ اس کا قلب امن اور ایمان سے بھر دے گا
غصہ پینے سے مراد معاف کر دینا ہے اور ایک حدیث میں ہے،
نادى مناد يوم القيامة اين الذين كان اجورهم على الله فلا يقوم الا من عفا
بروز قیامت ایک منادی ندا دے گا کہ وہ لوگ کہاں ہیں؟ جن کا اجر اللہ پر ہے اس ندا پر وہی شخص کھڑا ہوگا جس نے لوگوں کو

كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات معاف کر دیا ہوگا۔

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - ہم
ان دونوں روایات سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ معاف کرنا اللہ ، اور حبیب اللہ دونوں کے نزدیک پسندیدہ اور تقویت ایمان اور ترقی درجات کا ذریعہ ہے۔ بہر حال جب قاتل کو معاف کرنا مندوب اور باعث اجر و ثواب ہے تو اغلب یہ ہے کہ مقتول کا ولی قاتل کو معاف کر دے گا اور جب معاف کرنا اغلب ہے تو شہادت مفضی الی القتل نہ رہی اور جب شہادت مفضی الی القتل نہیں ہے تو یہ شہادت قبل کا سبب اور گواہ مسبب نہ ہوئے اس کے برخلاف مکرہ ( جس پر ا کراہ کیا گیا) ہے کہ جب اس کو کسی نے یہ دھمکی دی۔ اگر تو فلاں مثلاً شاہد کو قتل نہیں کرے گا تو ہم تجھ کو قتل کر دیں گے تو یہ اکراہ بالعموم مفضی الی القتل ہوگا کیونکہ بظاہر یہ ہے کہ مکرہ ( واصف ) اپنی زندگی کو ترجیح دے گا یعنی اپنی زندگی کی خاطر مکرہ ( واصف شاہد کو قتل کرنا گوارا کرے گا اور جب یہ بات ہے تو اکراہ مفضی الی القتل ہونے کی وجہ سے سبب قتل اور اکراہ کرنے والا ( عارف ) مسبب ہوا ۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ قصاصا مسبب قتل کیا جاتا ہے غیر مسبب قتل کو تل نہیں کیا جا تا پس گواہ جو مسبب قتل نہیں ہیں قصاصا ان کو قتل نہیں کیا جائیگا، اور مکرہ (اکراہ کرنے والا ) چونکہ مسبب قتل ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو قتل کیا جائے گا اور چونکہ اکراہ کرنے والا مسبب ہے اور گواہ مسبب نہیں ہیں اس لیے گواہوں کو اکراہ کرنے والے پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے قیاس کیا ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم اس بات کو تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ گواہ قاتل کے قتل کا سبب ہے لیکن فعل قل جو ولی قصاص کی طرف پایا گیا ہے وہ ولی کے اختیار صحیح سے پایا گیا ہے اور جو فعل کسی سے اس کے اختیار صحیح سے صادر ہوا ہو ۔ اس کی نسبت اسی کی طرف ہوتی ہے دوسرے کی طرف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس یہاں بھی فعل قتل کی نسبت ولی قصاص کی طرف ہوگی اور گواہوں کی طرف نہ ہوگی اور جب فعل قتل گواہوں کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے تو گواہ ، قاتل کو قصاصا قتل کرنے والے نہ ہوں گے اور جگئے قاتل کو قتل کرنے والے نہیں ہیں تو ان پر قصاص بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر یہ بھی تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ گواہوں کی طرف قتل کی نسبت منقطع نہیں ہوئی ہے بلکہ بحیثیت مسبب کے ان کی طرف قتل منسوب ہے تو پھر بھی گواہوں پر قصاص واجب ہونے میں شبہ ضرور ہے کیونکہ قاتل کے قتل کا حقیقی مرتکب تو ولی ہے اور گواہ سبب قتل ہیں۔ لہذا ایک اعتبار سے یعنی سبب قتل ہونے کے اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں اور ایک اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں اور ایک ، اعتبار سے ولی قاتل ہے اور جب ایک اعتبار سے ولی قاتل ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں تو گواہوں پر قصاص واجب ہونے میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور شبہ قصاص کو دور کر دیتا ہے۔ لہذا گواہوں پر سے قصاص دور کر دیا جائے گا یعنی ان پر قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ رہا یہ سوال کہ دیت چونکہ قصاص کا بدل ہے اور قصاص شبہ سے دور ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے دیت بھی شبہ سے دور ہو جانی چاہیے اور گواہوں پر قصاص کی طرح دیت بھی واجب ہونی چاہئے تھی تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دیت مالی شبہات کے ساتھ ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا دیت مالی ، شبہ کے باوجود گواہوں پر واجب ہو جائے گی اور قصاص جو شبہات سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کے ساقط ہونے سے دیت مالی ( جو شبہ سے ساقط نہیں ہوتی ) کا ساقط ہونالازم نہیں آئے گا۔
صاحب نامہ نے فرمایا کہ مکرہ یکسر الراء اکراہ کرنے والے پر) قصاص اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ گر فتح الراء ( جس پر اکراہ کیا گیا) کا اختیار فاسد ہوتا ہے اور مکرہ بکسر الراء کا اختیار صحیح ہوتا ہے اور اختیا مسیح کے مقابلے میں اختیار فاسد معدوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس مکرہ مافتح الراء، مکرہ بكسر الراء کیلئے بمنزلہ آلہ کے ہو گیا ہے اور فعل قتل جو کہ بفتح الراء کی طرف موجود ہوا ہے۔ وہ درحقیقت مکرم بكسر الراء کی
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10, page 159. Book of Retraction from Testimonies. ... So when the coerced person is prevented from this killing both by sacred law and custom, then coercion will not be more conducive to killing. In any case, it is established that testimony is greater than coercion in being a cause and conducive to killing. And in the case of coercion, the coercer, who is the efficient cause, will be killed in retaliation in the first degree. Our proof is that killing is the name of an action, and that action of killing was not performed by the witnesses. Rather, the perpetrator of the killing of the killer is the guardian of retaliation, and retaliation for killing the killer is not obligatory upon the guardian of retaliation. So when retaliation for killing the killer is not obligatory upon the guardian of retaliation, who is the perpetrator of the killing, then how can it be obligatory upon others, i.e., the witnesses, who did not perpetrate the killing? The conclusion is that after retracting their testimony, qisas for the killing of the killer will not be exacted from the witnesses. 'And likewise ... etc.' The author of al-Hidayah, while refuting the proof of Imam al-Shafi'i, said that the witnesses are not even the efficient cause preparing the killing of the killer, meaning their testimony is not the cause of killing, because the cause of an act is that which usually leads to that act. In summary, that which is conducive to a thing is its cause. And here the witnesses' testimony is not conducive to the killing, i.e., after their testimony, the killing of the killer is not inevitable, because forgiving the killer is recommended and desirable. Rather, in every matter, forgiveness and forbearance are approved and recommended in the eyes of the Shariah. Thus, regarding the mahr of an unconsummated divorcee, Allah Almighty says: 'And to forgive is nearer to piety' (al-Baqarah 237). The meaning is that if the man has paid the full mahr and then divorces before consummation, he should not take back half the mahr but leave the full mahr with the woman and forgive. And in Surah al-Ma'idah He says: 'And wounds are in retaliation, then whoever gives charity with it, it is an expiation for him' (al-Ma'idah 45). The meaning is that forgiving retaliation for wounds becomes an expiation for the person's sins, as is clarified in some hadiths. From these two verses, it is known that forgiveness and forbearance are approved and recommended in Islamic law. And in hadiths: 'Whoever suppresses anger while he has the power to execute it, Allah will fill his heart with security and faith.' Meaning of suppressing anger is forgiving. And in another hadith: 'A crier will call out on the Day of Resurrection: Where are those whose reward is upon Allah? None will stand except the one who forgives people.' From both these narrations, it is also known that forgiveness is approved by Allah and His beloved, and is a means of strengthening faith and raising ranks. In any case, when forgiving the killer is recommended and a cause of reward, then it is most likely that the guardian of the victim will forgive the killer. And when forgiveness is most likely, then testimony is no longer conducive to killing. And when testimony is not conducive to killing, then it is not a cause of killing, and the witnesses are not efficient causes. Contrary to the coerced person (the one coerced), when someone threatens him: 'If you do not kill so-and-so, we will kill you,' then this coercion is generally conducive to killing, because apparently the coerced person will prefer his own life, i.e., for the sake of his life, he will tolerate killing the witness. And when this is the case, coercion, due to being conducive to killing, becomes the cause of killing, and the coercer becomes the efficient cause. And it has already passed that in qisas, the efficient cause is killed; the non-efficient cause of killing is not killed. So the witnesses, who are not efficient causes of killing, will not be killed in qisas. And the coercer, since he is the efficient cause of killing, will be killed. And since the coercer is the efficient cause and the witnesses are not, therefore, analogy of witnesses to the coercer, as Imam al-Shafi'i made, is not correct. The second proof is that we accept that the witnesses are the cause of the killing of the killer, but the act of killing that occurred from the guardian of retaliation occurred with his valid choice. And an act that issues from someone with his valid choice is attributed to him, not to another. So here, the act of killing is attributed to the guardian, not to the witnesses. And when the act of killing is not attributed to the witnesses, then they are not the ones who killed the killer in qisas, and since they are not the killers, qisas is not obligatory on them. And even if we accept that the attribution of killing to the witnesses is not severed, but rather it is attributed to them as efficient causes, even then there is a doubt (shubha) in the obligation of qisas upon them, because the real perpetrator of the killing is the guardian, and the witnesses are the cause. Thus, from one aspect, i.e., being the cause, the witnesses are killers; from another aspect, the guardian is the killer. And when from one aspect the guardian is the killer and from another aspect the witnesses are killers, then a doubt arises in the obligation of qisas upon the witnesses. And doubt removes qisas. Therefore, qisas is removed from the witnesses, i.e., qisas is not obligatory upon them. As for the question that since diyah is the substitute for qisas, and qisas is removed by doubt, then diyah should also be removed by doubt, and diyah should have been obligatory on witnesses like qisas, the answer is that diyah (financial compensation) is established even with financial doubts. Thus, financial diyah will be obligatory upon the witnesses despite the doubt. And since qisas is removed by doubts, its removal does not necessitate the removal of financial diyah, which is not removed by doubt. The author of the marginalia (Sahib Namah) said: Qisas is obligatory upon the coercer (mukrih, with kasr of the ra) because the choice of the coerced (mukrah, with fatha of the ra) is corrupted, and the choice of the coercer is sound. And a corrupted choice is nullified in the presence of a sound choice. Thus, the coerced person becomes like a tool for the coercer. And the act of killing that originates from the coerced is, in reality, the act of the coercer.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute from the commentary on Al-Hidayah regarding the ruling on witnesses who retract their testimony after their testimony has led to the execution of qisas (retributive killing) of a murderer. The Hanafi position is that such witnesses are not liable for qisas, but they are liable for diyah (blood money). The passage refutes the Shafi'i position that analogizes witnesses to a coercer (mukrih) in cases of compulsion (ikrah). The argument proceeds in several steps. First, the author argues that testimony is not a cause (sabab) that necessarily leads to killing because the guardian of the victim may forgive the killer, which is recommended in Shariah. Quranic verses (al-Baqarah 2:237 and al-Ma'idah 5:45) and hadiths are cited to show that forgiveness is meritorious. Since forgiveness is likely, the testimony is not conducive to killing, so witnesses are not the efficient cause. This contrasts with coercion, where the coerced person is typically forced to kill to save his own life, making the coercion a cause and the coercer liable for qisas. Second, even if testimony is considered a cause, the act of killing is performed by the guardian with his valid choice, so attribution is to the guardian, not the witnesses. Third, even if attribution to witnesses as cause is accepted, there is a shubha (doubt) due to dual attribution (witness as cause, guardian as actor), and qisas is removed by shubha. However, diyah, being a financial obligation, persists despite shubha. The author also clarifies that the coercer (mukrih) is liable for qisas because his choice is sound, while the coerced (mukrah) acts with corrupted choice, becoming like a tool.

Key Terms
رجوع عن الشهادات (ruju' an al-shahadat): Retraction of testimony after judgment has been passed
مفضی الی القتل (mufdi ila al-qatl): That which leads to killing (as a consequence)
شبهہ (shubha): Doubt that prevents application of hadd and qisas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the liability of witnesses who retract their testimony after it has led to the execution of qisas?
A) They are liable for qisas (retributive killing).
B) They are liable for diyah (blood money) only.
C) They have no liability whatsoever.
D) They are liable for both qisas and diyah.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract after qisas pay diyah because testimony does not inevitably lead to killing, and shubha removes qisas but not financial liability.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Wakalah in Litigation: Must the Opponent Consent?
Inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute on wakalah bindingness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the requirement of the opponent's consent for wakalah in litigation, identify the exceptions, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Core Idea
Wakalah in litigation generally requires opponent's consent according to Abu Hanifa, but is binding without it per the Sahibayn and Shafi'i.

When you appoint a lawyer to sue someone, does the defendant have to accept your lawyer? This passage from the Hidayah reveals a key disagreement within the Hanafi school and with Imam al-Shafi'i. While all agree that appointing an agent is permissible, the debate centers on whether it becomes binding on the opponent without their consent. Understanding this dispute clarifies the rights of litigants and the limits of agency in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage discusses whether wakalah in litigation (khusumah) requires the consent of the opposing party (khasm) to be effective. Note that all agree on permissibility (jawaz); the dispute is about bindingness (luzum).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its exceptions
Abu Hanifa says wakalah is not binding without the opponent's consent, unless the principal is sick or absent on a journey of three days or more. Identify the rationale: the opponent is obligated to respond, and forcing a wakil could cause harm due to differing abilities.
The exception for sick/traveler arises because responding is not obligatory on them.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and Shafi'i) hold that wakalah is binding without consent. Their proof: appointing an agent is a disposition in one's own exclusive right, analogous to appointing an agent to collect debts.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy to debt collection because litigation imposes a burden on the opponent. He uses another analogy: a jointly owned slave where one owner's kitabah gives the other a choice, not a binding obligation.
The joint slave analogy (kitabah) shows that actions affecting another's rights require their consent.
5
Apply the exceptions: traveler, sick, and secluded woman
Whén the principal is sick or traveling, wakalah becomes binding even without consent. Furthermore, for a secluded woman (mukhaddara) who cannot appear in court, al-Razi and later scholars rule that wakalah is binding out of necessity.
This extension shows how later Hanafis leaned towards making agency binding in cases of hardship.

توکیل خصومت میں فریق مخالف کی رضا کا اعتبار کیا جائیگا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

وقال ابو حنيفة لا يجوز التوكيل بالخصومة من غير رضاء الخصم الا ان يكون المؤكل مريضا او غائبا مسيرة ثلاثة ايام فصاعدا وقالا يجوز التوكيل بغير رضاء الخصم وهو قول الشافعي ولا خلاف في الجواز انما الخلاف فى اللزوم لهما ان التوكيل تصرف فى خالص حقه فلا يتوقف على رضاء غيره كالتوكيل بتقاضى الديون وله ان الجواب مستحق على الخصم ولهذا يستحضره والناس متفاوتون في الخصومة فلو قلنا بلزومه يتضرر به فيتوقف على رضاه كالعبد المشترك اذا كاتبه احدهما يتخير الآخر بخلاف المريض والمسافر لان الجواب غير مستحق عليهما هنالك ثم كما يلزم التوكيل عنده من المسافر يلزم اذا اراد السفر لتحقق الضرورة ولو كانت المرأة مخدرة لم تجر عادتها بالبروز وحضور مجلس الحاكم قال الرازي يلزم التوكيل لانها لو حضرت لا يمكنها ان تنطق بحقها لحيائها فيلزم توكيلها قال وهذا شيء استحسنه المتأخرون

ترجمہ اور امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے خصومت کا وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ موکل بیمار ہو یا تین دن کی یا زیادہ کی مدت مسافت پر غائب ہو۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ بغیر تخصم کی رضامندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے، اور یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے، اور جائز ہونے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے بلکہ لازم ہونے میں اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے وکیل کرنا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے تو وہ غیر کی رضامندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا جیسے قرضے وصول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خصم پر جواب دہی لازم ہے اس وجہ سے مدعی خصم کو قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر کرائے گا۔ اور خصومت میں لوگوں کی حالتیں متفاوت ہیں، پس اگر ہم اس کے لزوم کے قائل ہو گئے تو اس سے دوسرے کو ضرر پہنچے گا، لہذا اس کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہے جیسے عبد مشترک، جب اس کو ایک مالک نے مکاتب کیا تو دوسرے کو اختیار ہو گا۔ برخلاف بیمار اور مسافر کے کیونکہ یہاں ان دونوں پر جواب دہی لازم نہیں ہے۔ پھر جسے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مسافر کی طرف سے تو کیل لازم ہوتی ہے ویسے ہی جب سفر کا ارادہ کرے تو لازم ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ضرورت متحقق ہے اور اگر کوئی پردہ نشین ہو اس کی عادت باہر نکلنے اور مجلس حاکم میں حاضر ہونے کہ نہ ہو تو
Appointing an agent in litigation: whether the consent of the opposing party is considered? Statements of the jurists. Abu Hanifa said: It is not permissible to appoint an agent in litigation without the consent of the opponent (khasm), unless the principal is sick or absent on a journey of three days or more. And the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is permissible to appoint an agent without the consent of the opponent, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. There is no disagreement regarding permissibility; the disagreement is only about bindingness (luzum). For them (the Sahibayn), agency is a disposition in one's own exclusive right, so it does not depend on the consent of another, like appointing an agent to collect debts. For him (Abu Hanifa), the opponent is obligated to respond (jawab), and for this reason the plaintiff summons him. People vary in their ability to litigate. If we say that agency is binding (necessary) on the opponent, he would be harmed. Therefore, it depends on his consent, like a jointly owned slave: when one owner executes a kitabah, the other has a choice. This is contrary to the case of a sick person or a traveler, because responding is not obligatory upon them there. Then, just as agency is binding from the traveler according to him, it is binding when he intends to travel, because necessity is realized. And if a woman is secluded (mukhaddara) and not accustomed to going out and attending the judge's court, al-Razi said: Agency is binding for her, because if she attended, she would not be able to speak her claim due to her shyness, so her agency is binding. He said: This is something approved by the later scholars.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of the opposing party's consent for wakalah in litigation (khusumah). It is an inter-madhhab dispute with intra-Hanafi elements. Imam Abu Hanifa requires the consent of the opponent (khasm) for the wakalah to be binding (lazim), unless the principal is sick or absent on a journey of three days or more. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that wakalah is valid and binding without the opponent's consent. The commentator clarifies that there is no disagreement on the permissibility (jawaz) of the wakalah itself; the dispute is about whether it is binding (luzum) on the opponent. The Sahibayn argue that appointing an agent is a disposition in one's own right, so it does not require anyone else's consent, analogous to appointing an agent to collect debts. Abu Hanifa argues that litigating imposes a burden on the opponent, who is obligated to respond. Since people have different abilities, allowing a binding wakalah without consent could harm the opponent. He draws an analogy with a jointly owned slave: if one owner makes a kitabah contract, the other owner is not bound by it and has a choice. However, this requirement of consent is waived if the principal is sick or traveling (absent for three days or more), because in those cases the opponent is not obligated to respond in the same way. The passage also extends the ruling to a woman who is secluded (mukhaddara) and not accustomed to appearing in court: according to al-Razi (a Hanafi jurist), it is binding for her to appoint an agent, and this is approved by later scholars (mutakkhirun). The commentary follows the author's order: first the statement of the dispute, then the proofs from both sides, then exceptions, then the extension to the secluded woman.

Key Terms
خصومت (khusumah): Litigation or legal dispute in court.
لزوم (luzum): Bindingness; whether the wakalah becomes obligatory for the opponent to accept.
جواب (jawab): The response or defense that the defendant must give in court.
مخدرہ (mukhaddara): A woman who is secluded and not accustomed to appearing in public, due to modesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is wakalah in litigation binding (lazim) without the opponent's consent?
A) Always binding
B) When the principal is sick or absent on a journey of three days or more
C) When the principal is a woman
D) Never binding

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on wakalah in litigation: Abu Hanifa requires the opponent's consent for bindingness unless the principal has an excuse; the Sahibayn hold it is always binding; later Hanafis made agency binding for a secluded woman showing a trend towards necessity-based exceptions.

Agency in Litigation: Opponent's Consent and Bindingness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bindingness of litigation agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether agency in litigation requires opponent's consent and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The dispute is not about permissibility but bindingness: Abu Hanifa says opponent's consent is needed for binding; Sahibayn say it is automatically binding.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding wakalah bil khusumah (agency in litigation). While all agree that appointing an agent is permissible, they differ on whether the opponent must accept the agent. Understanding this distinction is crucial for legal practice in Islamic courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that all jurists agree on permissibility (jawaz); the disagreement is solely on bindingness (luzum).
This is a common misconception.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and exceptions
Abu Hanifa holds that agency in litigation is not binding on the opponent without their consent, except when the principal is ill or a traveler (distance of three days or more).
The exceptions arise because the opponent cannot demand the principal's presence.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that agency is binding without the opponent's consent, analogizing it to agency for debt collection.
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the proofs
The Sahibayn argue agency is a disposition in one's pure right; Abu Hanifa responds that litigation involves the opponent's right to respond and harming them is possible.
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to a jointly owned slave in a kitabah contract.
5
Note the practical application (thamarah)
Under Abu Hanifa, the opponent can reject the agent; under the Sahibayn, the opponent must accept. The mufta bihi is generally Abu Hanifa's view.
For a secluded woman (mukhaddarah), the later scholars adopted bindingness as istihsan.

ترجمہ اور امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے خصومت کا وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ موکل بیمار ہو یا تین دن کی یا زیادہ کی مدت مسافت پر غائب ہو۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ بغیر تخصم کی رضامندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے، اور یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے، اور جائز ہونے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے بلکہ لازم ہونے میں اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے وکیل کرنا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے تو وہ غیر کی رضامندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا جیسے قرضے وصول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خصم پر جواب دہی لازم ہے اس وجہ سے مدعی خصم کو قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر کرائے گا۔ اور خصومت میں لوگوں کی حالتیں متفاوت ہیں ، پس اگر ہم اس کے لزوم کے قائل ہو گئے تو اس سے دوسرے کو ضرر پہنچے گا، لہذا اس کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہے جیسے عبد مشترک ، جب اس کو ایک مالک نے مکاتب کیا تو دوسرے کو اختیار ہو گا ۔ برخلاف بیمار اور مسافر کے کیونکہ یہاں ان دونوں پر جواب دہی لازم نہیں ہے۔ پھر جسے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مسافر کی طرف سے تو کیل لازم ہوتی ہے ویسے ہی جب سفر کا ارادہ کرے تو لازم ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ضرورت متحقق ہے اور اگر کوئی پردہ نشین ہو اس کی عادت باہر نکلنے اور مجلس حاکم میں حاضر ہونے کہ نہ ہو تو ابوبکر رازی نے کہا کہ اس کا وکیل کرنا لازم ہے، اس لئے وہ حاضر ہو بھی گئی تو اس کے لئے شرم کی وجہ سے اپنے حق کے ساتھ کلام کرنا ممکن نہ ہوگا ، لہذا اس کا وکیل کرنا لازم ہوگا۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ اس قول کو متاخرین نے مستحسن قرار دیا ہے۔
Regarding agency in litigation, whether the consent of the opponent is considered or not, sayings of the jurists. Abu Hanifa said: Agency in litigation is not permissible without the consent of the opponent unless the principal is ill or absent for a distance of three days or more. The Sahibayn said: Agency is permissible without the consent of the opponent, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. There is no dispute about permissibility; rather, the dispute is about bindingness. Their evidence: Agency is a disposition in one's pure right, so it does not depend on the consent of others, like agency to collect debts. His evidence: The opponent is obligated to respond, and that is why the plaintiff summons him to the court. And people vary in litigation; if we say it is binding, he would suffer harm, so it depends on his consent, like a shared slave when one partner makes a kitabah contract, the other partner has a choice. Unlike the ill and the traveler, because they are not obligated to respond there. Then, just as agency is binding in his view from the traveler, it is binding when he intends to travel because necessity is realized. And if a woman is secluded (mukhaddarah) and not accustomed to going out and attending the court of the judge, al-Razi said: Her agency is binding because even if she attended, she could not speak for her right due to shyness, so her agency is binding. He said: This is something that the later scholars considered good (istahsana).
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute in the Hanafi school regarding wakalah bil khusumah (agency in litigation). The central issue is whether appointing an agent to represent oneself in court requires the consent of the opposing party. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does not require consent for permissibility, but it is not binding (lazim) upon the opponent unless the principal is ill or traveling. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that it is binding even without consent, and this is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Marghinani, the author of al-Hidayah, clarifies that there is no disagreement on permissibility (jawaz); the dispute is on bindingness (luzum). Evidence for the Sahibayn: Agency is a disposition in one's own right, so it does not require another's consent, similar to appointing someone to collect debts. Evidence for Abu Hanifa: The opponent is obligated to respond to the case, and people differ in ability to litigate; forcing them to accept an agent could cause hardship. Therefore, the agency depends on the opponent's consent, by analogy to a jointly owned slave when one owner makes a kitabah contract—the other owner has an option. Exceptions: Illness or travel beyond three days, because the opponent cannot demand their presence. Further, if a traveler intends to travel, agency becomes binding due to necessity. Additionally, for a woman who is normally secluded (mukhaddarah) and not used to going to court, al-Razi stated that her agency is binding because even if she attends, she cannot speak due to shyness; the later scholars approved this as istihsan.

Key Terms
توکیل بالخصومة (tawkeel bil khusumah): Appointing an agent to represent oneself in litigation, either as plaintiff or defendant.
لزوم (luzum): Bindingness; the property of a contract or disposition that cannot be unilaterally revoked.
مخدرة (mukhaddarah): A woman who is secluded and does not normally go out in public, especially to court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does agency in litigation become binding (lazim) without the opponent's consent?
A) Only when the principal is a woman.
B) When the principal is ill or traveling a distance of three days or more.
C) Never, it is always non-binding.
D) When the principal is a merchant.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, agency in litigation is generally permissible without opponent's consent, but bindingness requires consent unless the principal is ill, traveling, or a secluded woman.

Dispute on Effect of Qadi's Ruling in Loan and Defect Return
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qadi's ruling effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi positions on the external and internal effect of a qadi's ruling in loan and sale rescission cases, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A qadi's ruling may be externally effective only or both externally and internally, depending on the subject matter.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a qadi's ruling in two distinct scenarios: a loan repayment dispute and a sale rescission due to defect. The key question is whether the qadi's ruling is effective only externally (zahiran) – meaning it can be reversed if an error appears – or both externally and internally (batinan), making it irreversible. Imam Abu Hanifa draws a distinction between the two cases, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) treat them alike. Additionally, there is a transmitted opinion from Imam Abu Yusuf favoring delay to protect the ruling's validity and show consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the passage discusses two distinct cases: a loan repayment where the debtor claims prior payment, and a sale rescission due to a hidden defect (return of a defective slave-girl). These form the basis of the ikhtilaf.
The loan case involves a simple property transfer order; the defect case involves a contract rescission.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in the loan case, the qadi's ruling is effective only externally (zahiran) – analogous to 'amlak mursalah' – so if an error appears, the property can be recovered. In the defect case, however, the ruling is effective both externally and internally (batinan) because it involves a contract rescission, making it irreversible once issued.
The key distinction is the type of legal act: simple property orders vs. contracts/rescissions.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that in both cases the ruling is only externally effective. Therefore, both are reversible if an error becomes apparent. Their evidence is that correction (tadarak) is possible in both scenarios, as the ruling can be annulled.
The Sahibayn do not distinguish between loan and defect cases; both are treated uniformly.
4
Note the additional view of some mashayikh on Imam Abu Yusuf's preference
Some later scholars transmit that Imam Abu Yusuf alone preferred delaying the decision in both cases: not giving the property or returning the goods without first taking an oath. This protects the qadi's ruling from being invalidated and shows consideration (shafaqat) for the debtor or seller.
This view represents a middle ground but is not the primary position of the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Imam Abu Hanifa, in the loan case, property can be recovered if error appears; in the defect case, the rescission stands permanently. Under the Sahibayn, both are reversible. Under Abu Yusuf's delay view, neither action is taken without an oath, avoiding potential error altogether.
The mufta bihi may depend on context; the Sahibayn's view is often preferred for its flexibility.

برخلاف قرضہ کا مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر قرضدار یہ دعوی کر دے کہ قرض خواہ اپنا قرضہ وصول کر چکا ہے تو قرض خواہ سے قسم لئے بغیر قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ مال قرض وکیل کو دے دے ان دونوں مسئلوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ قرض میں اگر قرض خواہ کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے وکیل کو مال قرض دینے کا غلط ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا تو اس کا تدارک ممکن ہے اس طور پر کہ جو مال وکیل کو دیا گیا تھا قرضدار اس سے اس مال کو
