Qada — Judiciary
beginner
6 min
Judge's Procedure After a Valid Claim: Confession, Evidence, and Oath
Lays out judge's procedure after valid claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step procedure a judge follows after a valid claim and identify the dalil for each step.

Core Idea
Confession binds; denial triggers evidence; lack of evidence gives plaintiff the right to demand an oath.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh of judicial procedure (qada) outlines the judge's duties once a valid claim is established. Understanding this sequence is crucial for knowing how rights are proven in court. The procedure is rooted in a famous hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
After a valid claim, the defendant may confess, deny, or be unable to provide evidence. The judge responds differently to each.
The three scenarios are: iqrār (confession), inkār (denial) with bayyinah, and inkār without bayyinah leading to yamīn.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
If the defendant confesses, the judge rules immediately; if he denies, the judge asks the plaintiff for evidence; if no evidence, the plaintiff may request an oath.
The confession is itself binding (wajib bi nafsihi) and does not require a judge's ruling to be effective.
3
Locate the dalīl
The hadith of Wā'il ibn Hujr (Bukhārī and Muslim) is cited: the Prophet asked the plaintiff for evidence, and when none was produced, he offered the defendant's oath.
The dalīl is a Sunnah ahad but sufficient for practice.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah
The phrase 'fakā lak yamīnuhu' (then you have his oath) shows the oath is the plaintiff's right, as the lām (possessive) indicates ownership.
This linguistic analysis supports the necessity of the plaintiff's request.
5
Note the condition: plaintiff's request
The judge does not automatically administer the oath; the plaintiff must request it. This is derived from the hadith's wording.
If the plaintiff does not request, the judge does not impose the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دعوی صحیح ہو جائے تو قاضی مدعی علیہ سے اس کے بارے میں سوال کرے تا کہ جہت حکم کھل جائے اگر مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا تو قاضی مدعی علیہ پر دعویٰ کا حکم کر بے گا
قال واذا صحت الدعوى سأل القاضى المدعى عليه عنها لينكشف وجه الحكم فان اعترف قضى عليه بها لان الاقرار موجب بنفسه فيأمر بالخروج عنه وان انكر سأل المدعى البيئة لقوله عليه السلام الك بينة فقال لا فقال لك يمينه سأل ورتب اليمين على فقد البيئة فلا بد من السؤال ليمكنه الاستحلاف قال وان أحضرها قضى بها لانتفاء التهمة عنها وان عجز عن ذلك و طلب يمين خصمه استحلفه عليها لما روينا ولا بد من طلبه لان اليمين حقه الا ترى انه كيف اضيف اليه بحرف اللام فلابد من طلبه
ترجمہ اور جب دعوی ہو گیا تو قاضی مدعی علیہ سے اس دعوی کے بارے میں دریافت کرے تا کہ حکم جہت کھل جائے پس اگر مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا تو قاضی مدعی علیہ پر اس دعوی کا حکم کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اقرار بذات خود موجب ہے پس قاضی اس کو حکم کرے گا کہ وہ اس اقرار کی ذمہ داری سے نکلنے اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے دعوی کا انکار کیا تو قاضی مدعی سے گواہ طلب کریگا کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مدعی سے فرمایا کیا تیرے پاس بینہ ہے۔ اس نے کہا نہیں پھر آپ نے فرمایا اب تیرے واسطے اس مدعی علیہ کی قسم ہے۔ آنحضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مدعی سے گواہ طلب کئے اور بینہ مفقود ہونے پر قسم کو مرتب فرمایا لہذا قاضی کا سوال کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ قاضی کے لئے مدعی علیہ سے لینا ممکن ہو سکے ۔ پس اگر مدعی نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو قاضی بینہ کے مطابق حکم کرے گا کیونکہ اس دعوی سے تہمت دور ہو گئی۔ اور اگر وہ اس سے عاجز آ گیا اور اس نے مدعی علیہ سے قسم طلب کی تو قاضی اس دعوی پر مدعی علیہ سے قسم لے گا۔ اس حدیث کیوجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی اور مدعی کا قسم طلب کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ قسم اسی کا حق ہے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ تم مدعی کی طرف حرف لام کے ساتھ کس طرح مضاف کی گئی ہے پس اس کا طلب کرنا ضروری ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب دعوی اپنی شرطوں کے ساتھ درست ہو گیا تو قاضی مدعی علیہ سے اس دعوی کے بارے میں دریافت کرے گا کہ تو اس دعوی کا اقرار کرتا ہے یا انکار کرتا ہے تاکہ قاضی اس دعوی کا مدعی علیہ پر حکم کرے گا کیونکہ اقرار بذات خود موجب اور حجت ہوتا ہے قضائے قاضی پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا ہے اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ انسان کو چونکہ اپنی ذات پر تمال ولایت حاصل ہے۔ اس لئے محض اس کے اقرار کر نے سے مدعی کا حق اس پر ثابت ہو جائے گا ۔ البتہ قاضی مدعی علیہ کو اس بات کا حکم دیگا کہ وہ اس حق کو ادا کر کے بری الذمہ ہو اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے اس دعوی کا انکار کیا تو اس دعوی کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے قاضی مدعی سے گواہ طلب کرے گا کیونکہ بخاری اور مسلم میں وائل بن حجر کی حدیث ہے کہ حضر موت سے ایک آدمی آیا اور ایک آدمی کندہ سے آیا۔ حضرمی نے کہا اے اللہ کے رسول (صلى الله عليه وسلم) اس کندہ نے میری زمین پر ظلما قبضہ کر لیا ہے کندہ نے کہا اللہ کے رسول (صلى الله عليه وسلم) یہ میری زمین ہے میرے قبضہ میں ہے میں اس میں زراعت کرتا ہوں اس کا اس میں کوئی حق نہیں ہے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرمی یعنی مدعی سے کہا کہ کیا تیرے پاس اس دعوی پر بینہ موجود ہے حضرمی نے کہا اللہ کے رسول ( ) بینہ تو موجود نہیں ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اب تیرے واسطے اس مدعی علیہ کی قسم ہے یعنی تیرے حق کی وجہ
When the claim is valid, the judge asks the defendant about it so that the aspect of judgment becomes clear. If the defendant confesses, the judge issues a ruling against him. He said (the matn): 'And when the claim is valid, the judge asks the defendant about it so that the aspect of judgment becomes clear. If he confesses, he rules against him by it because a confession is itself a cause; he orders him to exit from it. If he denies, he asks the plaintiff for evidence because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do you have evidence?' He said no; then he said: 'Then you have his oath.' He asked and placed the oath upon the absence of evidence. So the question is necessary to enable him to administer the oath. He said: 'And if he presents it, he rules by it because suspicion is removed from it. And if he is unable to do that and requests the oath of his opponent, he administers the oath to him on it based on what we narrated. And his request is necessary because the oath is his right. Do you not see how it is added to him with the letter lam? So his request is necessary.' Translation: And when the claim is made, the judge asks the defendant about this claim so that the aspect of judgment becomes clear. So if the defendant confesses, the judge rules against the defendant on this claim. Because confession is itself a cause, so the judge orders him to exit from the liability of this confession. And if the defendant denies the claim, the judge asks the plaintiff for witnesses because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the plaintiff: 'Do you have evidence?' He said no; then he said: 'Then you have his oath.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) asked the plaintiff for witnesses and placed the oath upon the absence of evidence. Therefore, the judge's question is necessary so that the judge can possibly administer the oath to the defendant. So if the plaintiff presents evidence, the judge rules according to it because suspicion is removed from this claim. And if he is unable to do that and he requests an oath from the defendant, the judge takes an oath from the defendant on this claim. Due to this hadith that we narrated, and the plaintiff's request for the oath is necessary because the oath is his right. Do you not see how it is added to him with the letter lam? So his request is necessary. Explanation: The scenario is that when the claim becomes valid with its conditions, the judge asks the defendant about the claim: 'Do you confess or deny it?' so that the judge can rule against the defendant on the claim. Because confession itself is a cause and a proof; it does not depend on the judge's ruling. The reason is that since a person has authority over himself, simply by his confession the plaintiff's right is established upon him. However, the judge orders the defendant to fulfill the right and become free of liability. And if the defendant denies the claim, to prove the claim the judge asks the plaintiff for witnesses because in Bukhari and Muslim there is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr: A man from Hadramawt came and a man from Kinda came. The Hadrami said: 'O Messenger of Allah, this Kindi has wrongfully seized my land.' The Kindi said: 'O Messenger of Allah, this is my land, in my possession, I cultivate it; he has no right in it.' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to the Hadrami, i.e., the plaintiff: 'Do you have evidence for this claim?' The Hadrami said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I have no evidence.' He said: 'Then you have his oath,' i.e., because of your right.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalīl naqlī) detailing the procedure a judge must follow after a valid claim is made. The text is structured around the matn (from al-Qudūrī or similar) and its Urdu translation/commentary. The procedure has three branches: (1) Confession (iqrār): If the defendant confesses, the judge immediately rules against him because confession is itself a binding proof; the judge only orders execution. (2) Denial (inkār): If the defendant denies, the judge asks the plaintiff for evidence (bayyinah) as per the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant' (al-bayyinatu ʿalā al-muddaʿī). The hadith of Wāʾil ibn Ḥujr from Bukhārī and Muslim is cited: a dispute over land where the Prophet asked the plaintiff for evidence; when none was produced, he offered the defendant's oath. (3) Oath (yamīn): If the plaintiff cannot produce evidence, he may request the defendant's oath. The judge then administers the oath. The plaintiff's request is necessary because the oath is his right (ḥaqq), as indicated by the possessive construction 'your oath' (yamīnuka). The commentary explains that confession does not require a judge's ruling to be effective; it binds the confessor directly. The hadith establishes the order: evidence first, then oath.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Confession by the defendant of the claim; it is a binding proof that obligates the defendant without requiring a judge's ruling.
إنكار (inkār): Denial of the claim by the defendant, which triggers the judge to ask the plaintiff for evidence.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of witnesses, required to prove a claim when the defendant denies.
يمين (yamīn): Oath taken by the defendant when the plaintiff lacks evidence; it is administered by the judge upon the plaintiff's request.
استحلاف (istiḥlāf): The act of the judge administering an oath to the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first step a judge takes after a valid claim is established and the defendant denies it?
A) Immediately administer an oath to the defendant
B) Ask the plaintiff to bring evidence
C) Rule in favor of the defendant
D) Ask the plaintiff to describe the property in detail

Key Takeaway
After a valid claim, the judge must follow a fixed sequence: if defendant confesses, rule; if denies, ask for evidence; if no evidence and plaintiff requests, administer oath.

Qada — Judiciary

General Rule: Bayyinah Precedes Yamin, Yamin Requires Plaintiff's Demand
Explains the procedure of first requiring bayyinah, then yamin upon plaintiff's request

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedural rule for administering an oath (yamin) in judicial claims and identify the condition that the plaintiff must demand the oath after failing to present evidence.

Core Idea
The oath is only administered after the plaintiff fails to provide evidence and demands the defendant's oath.

In Islamic judicial procedure, the burden of proof initially lies on the plaintiff. If the plaintiff presents evidence (bayyinah), the judge decides accordingly. If the plaintiff cannot produce evidence, the plaintiff may demand an oath from the defendant. This lesson explains the sequence and the necessity of the plaintiff's demand, supported by a hadith and Hanafi juridical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the judge's procedure? First, demand evidence from plaintiff. If evidence given, judge decides. If not, and plaintiff demands, administer oath to defendant.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the Prophet with the Hadhrami and Kindi, including the phrase 'laka yaminuhu'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'laka yaminuhu' attributes the oath to the plaintiff as a right, and the context shows oath only after evidence fails.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
This rule is agreed upon in the Hanafi school (muttafaq alayh).
5
Summarize the rule
Bayyinah is prior; yamin is conditional on plaintiff's failure to produce evidence and plaintiff's demand.

Source Text

كتاب الدعوى
۳۲۲
اشرف البدایہ جلد ہم
سے اس مدعی علیہ سے قسم لی جائے گی ۔ حضرمی نے کہا اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم یہ کندمی فاجر ، فاسق آدمی ہے جھوٹی قسم کھانے میں کوئی پرواہ نہیں کر ریگا اللہ کے رسول نے کہا تیرے لئے اس کے سواء کوئی حق نہیں ہے پس وہ کندمی یعنی مدعی علیہ جب قسم کھانے کے لئے چلا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اگر اس شخص نے ناحق طور سے مال کھانے کے لئے جھوٹی قسم کھائی تو قیامت میں اللہ اس سے ناراض ہو کر ملے گا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مدعی سے اولا بعینہ طلب کیا اور طر بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر قسم کو مرتب فرمایا حاصل یہ کہ قسم عدم بدینہ پر مرتب ہے اور جب قسم عدم بعینہ پر مرتب ہے تو قاضی پہلے مدگی سے بینہ کا سوال کرے گا تا کہ قاضی کے واسطے مدعی علیہ سے قسم لینا ممکن ہو سکے۔
صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر مدعی نے اپنے دعوی پر بینہ پیش کر دیا تو قاضی اس ببینہ کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے گا کیونکہ دعوی جس میں صدق اور کذب دونوں کا احتمال تھا بینہ کی وجہ سے جانب صدق رائج ہو گئی اور دعوی سے تہمت کذب دور ہو گئی اور جب بعینہ سے دعوای کا صادق ہونا راج ہو گیا تو قاضی بینہ کے مطابق مدعی کے لئے فیصلہ کر دے گا اور گر مدعی بینہ پیش کرنے سے عاجز آ گیا اور اس نے مدعی علیہ سے قسم کا مطالبہ کیا تو قاضی اس دعوئی پر مدعی علیہ سے قسم لے گا۔ دلیل وہی حدیث ہے جو او پر گذر چکی ہے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مدعلی علیہ سے قسم لینے کے لئے مدعی کا مطالبہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ قسم مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کا ایک حق ہے اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں سیمین کو حرف لام کے ساتھ مدعی کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے چنانچہ فرما یالک یمینه یعنی تیرے واسطے مدعلی علیہ کی قسم ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مدعلی علیہ کی قسم مدعی کا حق ہے۔ اور صاحب حق کو اس کا حق اس وقت دلایا جاتا ہے جب وہ طلب کرتا ہے پس اسی طرح جب مدعی اپنا حق یعنی یمین طلب کرے گا تو قاضی ، مدعی علیہ سے قسم دلائے گا۔
Book of Claims. ... from this defendant an oath will be taken. The Hadhrami said: O Messenger of Allah, this Kindi is a wicked, immoral man who does not care about swearing a false oath. The Messenger of Allah said: You have no right except this. Then when the Kindi, i.e., the defendant, went to take the oath, the Prophet said: If this person swears a false oath to consume wealth unjustly, Allah will meet him angry on the Day of Judgment. From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet first demanded evidence from the plaintiff, and when there was no evidence, he assigned the oath to him. The conclusion is that the oath is conditioned upon the absence of evidence. When that is the case, the judge will first ask the plaintiff for evidence so that it becomes possible for the judge to take an oath from the defendant. Sahib al-Quduri said: If the plaintiff presents evidence for his claim, the judge will decide according to it, because the claim, which was probable of truth and falsehood, becomes confirmed as true by the evidence, and the suspicion of falsehood is removed. When truth becomes preponderant through evidence, the judge decides for the plaintiff. If the plaintiff is unable to present evidence and demands an oath from the defendant, the judge will take an oath from the defendant regarding the claim. The proof is the same hadith mentioned above. Sahib al-Hidayah says: For taking an oath from the defendant, the plaintiff's demand is necessary because the oath is a right of the plaintiff against the defendant. The evidence for this is that in the hadith, the oath is attributed to the plaintiff with the letter 'lam', as it says: 'Laka yaminuhu' (the oath is for you). From this it is understood that the defendant's oath is a right of the plaintiff. A right is only granted when demanded. Thus, when the plaintiff demands his right, i.e., the oath, the judge will administer the oath to the defendant.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa). It establishes the procedural rule: the judge first asks the plaintiff to produce evidence (bayyinah). If the plaintiff has evidence, judgment is given accordingly. If the plaintiff is unable to present evidence and then demands an oath (yamin) from the defendant, the judge administers the oath to the defendant. The proof is the famous hadith of the Prophet with the Hadhrami and Kindi, where the Prophet first asked for the plaintiff's evidence, and only when none was provided did he refer to the defendant's oath. Additionally, the commentator (Sahib al-Hidayah) emphasizes that the plaintiff must demand the oath because it is his right, citing the phrase 'laka yaminuhu' (the oath is for you). This demand is necessary for the judge to act.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically two witnesses or equivalent proof presented by the plaintiff.
یمین (yamin): An oath taken by the defendant when the plaintiff lacks evidence.
مدعی (mudda'i): The plaintiff, the one who brings a claim.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayh): The defendant, the one against whom the claim is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the judge to administer an oath to the defendant in a claim?
A) The plaintiff must provide evidence first.
B) The plaintiff must demand the oath after failing to present evidence.
C) The defendant must request the oath.
D) The judge may administer the oath even without the plaintiff's demand.

Key Takeaway
The judge must first demand evidence from the plaintiff; only upon the plaintiff's failure to provide evidence and subsequent demand for an oath does the judge administer the oath to the defendant.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Oath Demand When Witnesses Are in the City
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istihlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the defendant's oath when the plaintiff claims witnesses are present in the city, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each position.

Core Idea
If witnesses are in the city, Abu Hanifa denies the oath; Abu Yusuf grants it.

In the Hanafi school, a key procedural question arises: when a plaintiff asserts that their witnesses are present in the city but demands the defendant's oath instead of producing them, should the judge administer the oath? This lesson unpacks the ikhtilaf (disagreement) among the three primary Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute clarifies the nature of the oath as either a substitute for evidence or an independent right of the plaintiff.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
The plaintiff says 'I have bayyinah hadirah (witnesses present)' and demands the defendant's oath (istihlaf). The judge must decide whether to administer the oath or force the plaintiff to produce the witnesses.
The phrase 'hadirah' is ambiguous: in the courtroom or in the city? The author clarifies it means in the city.
2
State the positions of the three imams
Abu Hanifa: no oath. Abu Yusuf: oath. Muhammad: two narrations (one with each of the previous).
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil) of each side
Abu Hanifa argues that the oath is conditional on inability to produce evidence (based on the hadith where the Prophet only offered the oath after the plaintiff had no witnesses). Abu Yusuf argues that the oath is an independent right of the plaintiff, proven by the hadith 'laka yaminuhu'.
The difference hinges on whether the oath is a substitute for evidence or a parallel remedy.
4
Examine the meaning of 'bayyinah hadirah'
The author clarifies that 'hadirah' means present in the city, not in the courtroom. If witnesses are in the courtroom, there is consensus that no oath is taken because evidence is immediately available.
This semantic clarification is crucial to understanding the dispute.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the plaintiff must produce the witnesses; no oath is given. Under Abu Yusuf's view, the plaintiff can opt for the oath immediately, delaying or avoiding witness production.
The mufta bihi (operative position) in the school is often Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

پس جب مدعی ، مدعی علیہ سے قسم کا مطالبہ کرے گا تو مدعی علیہ اس کو قبول کرے گا اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین میں حق کا ثبوت اقامت بینہ سے عاجز ہونے پر مرتب ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے پس اقامت بینہ سے بجز کے بغیر قسم مدگی کا حق نہ ہوگی جیسا کہ جب بینہ مجلس قاضی میں موجود ہو اور امام محمد امام خصاف کے بیان کے مطابق ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں اور طحاوی کے بیان کے مطابق ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں۔

Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. Chapter of the Oath. Translation: This chapter is about the oath. Book of Claims. Commentary: It has passed before that when the defendant denies the claim and the plaintiff is unable to present evidence and demands the oath, the oath becomes obligatory upon the defendant. So the author has mentioned in this chapter the rulings related to the oath. When the plaintiff says: I have witnesses present and demands the oath, is the demand valid? Statements of the jurists: 'And when the plaintiff says: I have bayyinah present and demands the oath, he will not be sworn according to Abu Hanifa, meaning present in the city. And Abu Yusuf said: He will be sworn because the oath is his right by the famous hadith. So when he demands it, he must be answered. And for Abu Hanifa is that the establishment of the right in the oath is conditioned upon inability to produce evidence, due to what we narrated. So it is not his right without it, just as when the evidence is present in the court. And Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf according to what al-Khasaf mentioned, and with Abu Hanifa according to what al-Tahawi mentioned.' Translation: And when the plaintiff said: I have bayyinah present, and he demanded the oath from the defendant, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the oath will not be taken from the defendant, meaning the witnesses are present in the city. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that the oath will be taken because the oath is a right of the plaintiff, established by the famous hadith. So when the plaintiff demands it from the defendant, the defendant must accept it. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the establishment of the right in the oath is conditioned upon being unable to produce evidence, due to the hadith we narrated. So the oath is not the plaintiff's right without (inability to produce) evidence, just as when the evidence is present in the court. And Imam Muhammad, according to al-Khasaf's narration, is with Abu Yusuf, and according to al-Tahawi's narration, with Abu Hanifa. Commentary: The scenario is: if the plaintiff says 'my witnesses are present' and demands the oath from the defendant, then according to Abu Hanifa, the oath will not be taken from the defendant; according to Abu Yusuf, it will be taken. Sahib al-Hidayah says that 'present' means the witnesses are present in the city, not that they are present in the court. Because if they are present in the court, there is consensus that the oath is not taken. But if the plaintiff says they are present in the city, there is ikhtilaf. Imam (Abu Hanifa) says the oath is not taken; Abu Yusuf says it will be taken. Abu Yusuf's proof is the famous hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara' or the earlier mentioned 'laka yaminuhu', which proves that the oath is the plaintiff's right. So when the plaintiff demands his right, i.e., the oath, the judge...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) within the chapter on oaths (Bab al-Yamin) of the Book of Claims. The specific issue: if the plaintiff says 'I have witnesses present (in the city)' and demands the defendant's oath, should the judge administer the oath? Imam Abu Hanifa says no, because the right to the oath is conditional upon the plaintiff's inability to produce evidence. Since evidence is available in the city, the oath cannot be taken. Imam Abu Yusuf says yes, because the oath is an independent right of the plaintiff, proven by the hadith 'laka yaminuhu'. Imam Muhammad has two narrations: one with Abu Yusuf (as reported by al-Khasaf) and one with Abu Hanifa (as reported by al-Tahawi). The commentary clarifies that 'present' means in the city, not in the courtroom; if witnesses were in court, there is consensus that no oath is taken. The Hanafi position is that the judge must consider the accessibility of witnesses.

Key Terms
بینہ حاضرة (bayyinah hadirah): Witnesses present in the city (according to the context, not in the courtroom).
استحلاف (istihlaf): Administering an oath to the defendant at the plaintiff's demand.
یمین (yamin): Oath sworn by the defendant in denial of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a plaintiff says 'I have witnesses present in the city' and demands the defendant's oath, what should the judge do?
A) Administer the oath to the defendant because the plaintiff has a right to it.
B) Not administer the oath because the plaintiff should first bring the witnesses.
C) Administer the oath only if the defendant agrees.
D) Ask the plaintiff to prove that the witnesses are actually in the city.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the defendant's oath is not administered when the plaintiff claims to have witnesses in the city, because the oath is conditional on inability to produce evidence.

Oath Demand When Plaintiff Has Witnesses in City
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath demand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on demanding an oath when the plaintiff claims to have witnesses in the city, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
If the plaintiff has witnesses in the city, the oath is not administered — the right to demand the oath is conditional on inability to produce evidence.

Imagine a plaintiff who says 'I have witnesses in the city' but demands the defendant take an oath. Should the judge swear the defendant? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. Abu Hanifa says no, because the plaintiff can bring the witnesses; Abu Yusuf says yes, because the oath is the plaintiff's right by hadith. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The plaintiff declares he has 'present evidence' (bayyinah ḥāḍirah) but demands the defendant's oath. The key question: should the judge administer the oath?
The term 'present' is interpreted by Abu Hanifa as present in the city, not necessarily in court.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa: the defendant is not sworn. The right to demand the oath is conditional on inability to present witnesses. Since the plaintiff can produce them, the oath is not his right.
Analogy: if witnesses are present in the court, no oath is demanded.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf: the defendant should be sworn because the oath is the plaintiff's absolute right per the hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara'.
He sees the hadith as unconditional.
4
Note Muhammad's two narrations
Imam Muhammad has two narrations: one with Abu Yusuf (reported by al-Khassaf), one with Abu Hanifa (reported by al-Tahawi).
This shows the issue was debated even among the direct students.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's position: the defendant is not sworn. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah gives tarjih to Abu Hanifa's view.
Practical consequence: the judge orders the plaintiff to bring his witnesses instead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذاقال المدعى لى بينة حاضرة وطلب اليمين لم يستحلف عند ابي حنيفة معناه حاضرة في المصر وقال ابويوسف يستحلف لان اليمين حقه بالحديث المعروف فاذا طالبه به يجيبه ولابي حنيفة ان ثبوت الحق في اليمين مرتب على العجز عن اقامة البيئة لما روينا فلا يكون حقه دونه كما اذا كانت البيئة حاضرة في المجلس ومحمد مع ابي يوسف فيما ذكره الخصاف ومع ابي حنيفة فيما ذكر الطحاوى
And when the plaintiff said: 'I have present evidence' and demanded the oath, he is not sworn (the defendant is not made to swear) according to Abu Hanifa. Its meaning: 'present in the city.' Abu Yusuf said: He is sworn because the oath is his right by the well-known hadith, so when he demands it, he (the defendant) responds. And for Abu Hanifa: The establishment of the right in the oath is conditional upon inability to present evidence, as we have narrated, so it is not his right without it, just as when evidence is present in the court session. And Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf according to what al-Khassaf mentioned, and with Abu Hanifa according to what al-Tahawi mentioned.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a plaintiff who states that he has witnesses (bayyinah) present in the city (al-misr) and demands that the defendant take an oath (yamin). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the defendant is not to be sworn, because the plaintiff's right to demand an oath is subordinate to his inability to produce witnesses. Since the witnesses are available in the city, the plaintiff is not incapable of presenting evidence, so the oath is not his right. This is analogous to the case where witnesses are physically present in the court session (al-majlis), where all agree the oath is not to be administered. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the defendant should be sworn because the oath is the plaintiff's right based on the hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara' (the burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the denier). Therefore, when the plaintiff demands his right (the oath), the defendant must comply. Regarding Imam Muhammad, there are two narrations: according to al-Khassaf, he agrees with Abu Yusuf; according to al-Tahawi, he agrees with Abu Hanifa. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: the oath is not administered when the plaintiff has witnesses in the city.

Key Terms
بينة حاضرة (bayyinah ḥāḍirah): Present evidence; witnesses that the plaintiff claims are available in the city (al-misr) or in the court.
يمين (yamīn): Oath taken by the defendant to deny the claim when the plaintiff has no evidence.
استحلاف (istiḥlāf): The act of the judge administering an oath to the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the defendant not sworn when the plaintiff says he has witnesses in the city?
A) Because the plaintiff has no right to demand an oath at all.
B) Because the oath is only for the defendant, never for the plaintiff.
C) Because the plaintiff's right to the oath is conditional on his inability to produce witnesses, and here he has witnesses available.
D) Because the witnesses are not in the court session.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view that the oath is not administered when the plaintiff has witnesses in the city.

The Oath is Never Returned to the Plaintiff
Hanafi ruling with proof and Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the oath is never returned to the plaintiff, explain the proof from the hadith, and contrast the Shafi'i position with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
The oath is exclusively for the denier; division precludes partnership—no oath for the plaintiff.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar lays down a foundational rule of Hanafi court procedure: the oath is never administered to the plaintiff. The proof is a clear Prophetic division of roles. A major inter-madhhab dispute arises with the Shafi'i school, which allows returning the oath under certain circumstances. Understanding this dispute reveals how a single hadith can generate divergent rulings through different interpretive principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
The passage begins by stating the ruling: 'The oath is not returned to the plaintiff.' Identify that this is a negative statement prohibiting the act of offering the oath to the claimant.
This is a categorical prohibition; no exceptions.
2
Analyze the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is the hadith: 'The evidence is upon the claimant, and the oath is upon the denier.' The Hanafi interpretation focuses on two linguistic features: (1) the definite article 'al' in 'al-yamin' indicating the entire genus, and (2) the division (qism) between claimant and denier, which precludes sharing (shirkah).
Linguistic precision is key: the genus is fully assigned to the denier.
3
Understand the Shafi'i Opposition
Identify the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i allows the oath to be returned to the plaintiff if the defendant refuses or if the plaintiff has only one witness. The basis is other Prophetic practices and qiyas.
This opposition is explicitly mentioned in the text.
4
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: In a Hanafi court, if the defendant refuses to swear, the judge treats that refusal (nukul) as an admission and rules for the plaintiff without any oath from him. In a Shafi'i court, the defendant's refusal leads to the plaintiff being asked to swear.
Different procedures, same goal—but the burden of oath shifts.
5
Confirm the Tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the plain apparent meaning (zahir) of the hadith and the principle that division precludes partnership. The exceptions claimed by Shafi'i are not considered sufficiently proven. Hence the mufta bihi is the absolute prohibition.
No intra-Hanafi dispute; all three imams agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا ترد اليمين على المدعى لقوله عليه السلام البينة على المدعى واليمين على من انكر قسم والقسمة تنافى الشركة وجعل جنس الايمان على المنكرين وليس وراء الجنس شيء و فيه خلاف الشافعي
He (al-Quduri) said: And the oath is not returned to the plaintiff because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The evidence is upon the plaintiff and the oath is upon the one who denies.' He (the Prophet) divided, and division precludes partnership, and he made the genus of oaths upon the deniers, and there is nothing beyond the genus. And in this there is a difference with al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar stating a fundamental principle: the oath is never returned to the plaintiff (la turaddu al-yaminu 'ala al-mudda'i). The proof is the hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara' (The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the denier). The author (al-Quduri) explains that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a division (qism) between plaintiff and defendant: the plaintiff must produce evidence, the defendant must swear. Division precludes partnership (shirkah), meaning that what belongs to one cannot belong to the other. The Prophet used the generic term 'al-yamin' (the oath) with the definite article indicating the entire genus, and he assigned this entire genus to the deniers. Thus there is no part of the oath left for the plaintiff. Therefore, under no circumstances is the oath to be administered to the plaintiff. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. According to the Shafi'i school, if the defendant refuses to take the oath or has no evidence, the oath may be returned to the plaintiff. For example, if the defendant (denier) refuses to swear, the plaintiff may be asked to swear, and if he does, judgment is given in his favor. Similarly, if the plaintiff has only one witness and is unable to produce a second, he may swear an oath (yamin al-qada') to supplement the single witness. This view is also attributed to Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad in one narration. The Hanafi school, however, emphatically rejects the return of the oath to the plaintiff, adhering to the plain division in the hadith.

Key Terms
رد اليمين (raddu al-yamīn): Returning the oath to the plaintiff after the defendant refuses to swear or is unable.
جنس الأيمان (jinsu al-aymān): The genus/category of oaths; the Prophet made the entire genus belong to the deniers.
القسمة تنافى الشركة (al-qismatu tanāfī al-shirkah): Division precludes partnership; if something is divided between two parties, it cannot be shared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on returning the oath to the plaintiff?
A) It is permissible if the defendant refuses.
B) It is never permissible.
C) It is permissible only if the plaintiff has one witness.
D) It is recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
The oath belongs exclusively to the denier; division precludes sharing, so the plaintiff can never be asked to swear.

The Oath is Not Returned to the Plaintiff (Hanafi View)
Ruling that oath belongs exclusively to defendant, with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for not returning the oath to the plaintiff and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The hadith divides proof and oath — division precludes transfer.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri states the Hanafi position that the oath is exclusively the defendant's right. The proof is the Prophetic hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies.' The Hanafi school argues that this division (qasamah) implies exclusivity, so the oath cannot be returned to the plaintiff. We will explore the linguistic argument and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The oath is never returned to the plaintiff, regardless of whether the defendant refuses or the plaintiff has one witness.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Identify the dalil
The hadith: 'Al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara.'
Reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyse the Hanafi wajh al-dalalah
The word 'ala indicates allocation, and the definite article 'al' indicates the genus, making oath exclusive to deniers. Division (qasamah) implies no partnership.
Thus the oath belongs entirely to the defendant.
4
State the Shafi'i position
If the defendant refuses to swear, or if the plaintiff has one witness, the oath is returned to the plaintiff.
Similar view from Malik and Ahmad in one narration.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response
The division in the hadith is absolute. The case of one witness plus oath is an exception based on specific evidence (yamin ma'a al-shahid) and does not generalize.
Defendant's refusal leads to default judgment, not transfer.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, if defendant refuses, judge rules against him without plaintiff swearing. Under Shafi'i, plaintiff may swear and win the case.
Practical consequence of the dispute.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام محمد سے دو روایتیں ہیں چنانچہ امام خصاف کی روایت کے مطابق امام محمد امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں اور امام طحاوی کی روایت کے مطابق امام محمد امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں غالیہ البیان میں صاحب ہدایہ پر اعتراض کرتے ہوئے کہا گیات کے کہ امام محمد کا قول نہ تو خصاف نے نقل کیا ہے اور نہ طحاوی نے نقل کیا ہے لیکن صاحب ہدایہ نے ان دونوں بزرگوں کے حوالہ سے امام محمد کا قول نہ جانے کہاں سے نقل کر دیا ہے واللہ اعلم ۔
قسم مدعی پر نہیں لوٹائی جائے گی
قال ولا ترد اليمين على المدعى لقوله عليه السلام البينة على المدعى واليمين على من انكر قسم والقسمة تنافى الشركة وجعل جنس الايمان على المنكرين وليس وراء الجنس شيء و فيه خلاف الشافعي ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا کہ یمین ، مدعی پر نہیں لوٹائی جائے گی کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے مدعی پر مبینہ ہے اور منکر پر نہین ہے اللہ کے رسول نے تقسیم فرمائی ہے اور تقسیم ، شرکت کے منافی ہے اور جنس ایمان کو منکرین پر مقرر کیا اور جنس کے علاوہ کوئی چیز باقی نہیں ہے اور اس حکم میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ مدعی پر کسی بھی حال میں قسم نہیں ہے یعنی ایسا کبھی نہیں ہوگا کہ مدعی کے محض قسم کھانے پر قاضی اس کے حق میں حکم صادر کر دے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان دو چیزوں کو تقسیم فرمایا ہے یعنی مدعی پر مبینہ مقرر کیا ہے اور مالی عالیہ پر قسم مقرر کی ہے اور تقسیم ، شرکت کے منافی ہے۔ پس رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے الیمین کو الف لام جنس کے ساتھ ذکر فرما کر جنس قسم، منکر یعنی مدنی علیہ پرلا گو کی ہے اور جنس کے علاوہ کوئی اور چیز باقی نہیں ہے۔ لہذا جب جنسی قسم مدعی علیہ کے ساتھ مختص ہو گئی تو اب قسم کا کوئی حصہ ایسا نہیں رہا جو مدعی کے واسطے ہو۔ اور جب مدعی کے واسطے قسم کا کوئی حصہ نہیں رہا تو مدعی پر قسم بھی نہ آئے گی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس حکم میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب بدگی کے پاس بالکل گواہ نہ ہوں اور قاضی نے مدعلی علیہ کو قسم ا فی لیکن اس نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قسم مدعی کی طرف عود کرے گی ۔ پس اگر مدعی نے قسم کھائی تو قاضی اس کی قسم پر اس کے حق میں فیصلہ صادر کر دے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر مدعی نے ایک گواہ پیش کیا اور دوسرے گواہ سے عاجز ہوا تو بھی مدعی کی طرف قسم عود کرے گی ۔ چنانچہ اس گواہ کے ساتھ اگر مدعی قسم کھا گیا تو قاضی اس کے حق میں فیصلہ صادر کر دے گا۔ اور اگر مدعی نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو مدیقی کے حق میں فیصلہ نہ ہوگا یہی ایک روایت امام مالک اور امام احمد کی ہے۔
The plaintiff shall not be made to take an oath. For the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies.' He made a division, and division is contrary to partnership. He placed the genus of oaths upon the deniers, and beyond the genus there is nothing. And in this there is a difference of opinion with al-Shafi'i. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said that the oath is not returned to the plaintiff in any case, because the Prophet divided two things between the plaintiff and the defendant: he assigned the proof to the plaintiff and the oath to the defendant. Division is contrary to partnership. He mentioned 'al-yamin' with the definite article for the genus, making the genus of oath specific to the defendant (the denier), and there is nothing left beyond the genus. Therefore, when the oath by genus is made exclusive to the defendant, no part of the oath remains for the plaintiff. So the plaintiff is not to take an oath. The author says that in this ruling there is a difference with al-Shafi'i. He says that when the plaintiff has no witnesses at all and the judge calls upon the defendant to swear but he refuses, then the oath reverts to the plaintiff. If the plaintiff then swears, the judge will decide in his favor. Similarly, if the plaintiff produces one witness and is unable to produce a second, the oath also reverts to him. So along with that witness, if he swears, the judge will decide in his favor. If the plaintiff refuses to swear, no decision is given in his favor. This is also a narration from Malik and Ahmad.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam al-Quduri's matn stating that the oath (yamin) is never returned to the plaintiff. It is followed by a commentary that explains the proof from the hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies.' The Hanafi school interprets this hadith as a division (qasamah) of two distinct functions: the plaintiff must provide evidence, the defendant must swear. Since division implies exclusivity—like dividing a property between partners—the oath becomes the exclusive right of the defendant. Therefore, if the defendant refuses to swear, the plaintiff cannot be made to swear instead; instead, the defendant is defaulted and a decision is made against him. The text then notes a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that if the defendant refuses to swear, the oath is returned to the plaintiff. There is also an intra-Hanafi discussion: Imam Muhammad has two narrations—one supporting Abu Yusuf (and thus the view that the oath is not returned) and one supporting Abu Hanifa (allowing return in certain cases). However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the oath is not returned. The commentary also mentions that this is the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad in one narration. The key point is that the Hanafi school strictly separates the roles of plaintiff and defendant, preventing the transfer of the oath.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath sworn by the defendant to deny the claim. In this context, it is a right of the defendant.
مدعي (mudda'i): The plaintiff who brings a claim against another. He must produce evidence (bayyinah) to support his claim.
مدعى عليه (mudda'a 'alayh): The defendant against whom the claim is made. He must either admit or deny, and if he denies, he is required to take an oath.
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females, or other acceptable proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence if the defendant refuses to take the oath?
A) The plaintiff must swear.
B) The judge decides against the defendant.
C) The case is dismissed.
D) The plaintiff is given a second chance to produce evidence.

Key Takeaway
The oath is a right of the defendant and cannot be transferred to the plaintiff; the judge must decide against the defendant if he refuses to swear.

Preference of External Claimant's Evidence in Absolute Ownership
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on evidence preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on evidence in absolute ownership claims, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Possession already proves ownership; the external claimant's evidence adds new proof, so it is preferred.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, as explained in Al-Hidayah, presents a key ruling in judicial procedure: when both parties bring evidence but one is in possession, who wins? The Hanafi school distinguishes between absolute ownership (no cause given) and restricted ownership (cause given). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that in absolute ownership (milk mutlaq), the external claimant's evidence (bayyinatu al-kharij) is preferred over the possessor's evidence.
This is the default ruling from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the possessor's evidence is stronger because possession strengthens its apparent truth.
He analogizes to cases like offspring and marriage.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i's proof is based on qiyas: just as in offspring and marriage claims the possessor's evidence is accepted, here too possession should tip the scale.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response shows that the analogy fails because in offspring and marriage, possession does not specifically indicate the claimed fact (e.g., that the animal was born from a particular female), whereas in absolute ownership, possession directly indicates ownership.
Hence the external claimant's evidence provides new, specific proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the Hanafi view, the external claimant wins; under the Shafi'i view, the possessor wins. This is the practical consequence for judges.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - دہم
۳۲۵
ملک مطلق میں قابض کے بینہ قبول نہ ہوں گے اور غیر قابض کے بینہ اولی ہیں
كتاب الدعوى
قال ولا تقبل بينة صاحب اليد فى الملك المطلق وبينة الخارج اولى وقال الشافعي يقضى ببينة ذى اليد لاعتضادها باليد فيقوى الظهور وصار كالنتاج والنكاح ودعوى الملك مع الاعتاق او الاستيلاد او التدبير ولنا ان بينة الخارج أكثر اثباتا او اظهارا لان قدر ما اثبته اليد لا يثبته بينة ذى اليد اذا اليد دليل مطلق الملك بخلاف النتاج لان اليد لا تدل عليه وكذا على الاعتاق و اختيه وعلى الولاء الثابت بها ترجمہ . صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ ملک مطلق میں قابض کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا اور غیر قابض کا بینہ اولی ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قابض کے بینہ پر فیصلہ ہوگا کیونکہ قبضہ کی وجہ سے بعینہ قوی ہو گیا لہذا ظہور بھی قوی ہوگا اور یہ نتائج اور نکاح اور دعوی ملک مع الاعتاق یا مع اللہ بیر کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر قابض کا بینہ زیادہ مثبت یا زیادہ مظہر ہے کیونکہ جس قدر قبضہ نے ثابت کیا ہے قابض کے بعینہ نے اس کا بھی ثابت نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے کہ قبضہ تو مطلق ملک کی دلیل ہے برخلاف آج کے کیونکہ قبضه تا حملات می تابان طرح اعتناق اور استیلا دونہ یہ اور اس ولاء پر جو ان سے ثابت ہوتی ہے بندہ دلالت نہیں مرتاب۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص مال معین پر قابض ہے اور اس پر ایک غیر تیا بعض نے دعوئی کیا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں، ایک تو یہ کہ اس نے ملک مقید کا دعوی کیا یعنی ملک کا دعوی کیا اور مالک ہونے کا سبب بھی ذکر کیا مثلاً یہ کہا کہ یہ غلام جس پر یہ شخص قابض ہے میرا ہے اور میرا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ یہ میری ملک میں میری باندی سے پیدا ہوا ہے یا یہ بیل میرا ہے کیونکہ یہ میری مملوکہ گائے سے میری ملک میں پیدا ہوا ہے۔
-۲۔ دوم یہ کہ اس نے ملک مطلق کا دعوی کیا یعنی ملک کا دعوی تو کیا لیکن مالک ہونے کا سبب بیان نہیں کیا مثلا یہ کہا کہ یہ چیز میری ملک ہے اور اس قابض کے قبضہ میں ناحق طور پر ہے پس ملک مطلق کی صورت میں اگر قابض نے اپنے مالک ہونے پر بینہ پیش کیا اور غیر قابض نے اپنے مالک ہونے پر بینہ پیش کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک غیر قابض کا بینہ اولی ہوگا لہذا وہی قبول ہوگا اور غیر تقابض کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔
حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قابض کے گواہ قبول ہوں گے اور اس کے حق میں فیصلہ کیا جائے گا کیونکہ قابض کی گواہی اس کے قربننہ کی وجہ سے قوی ہو گئی ہے۔ اور جب قابض کی گواہی قوی ہوگئی ، تو اس سے حق کا ظہور بھی قوی ہوگا اور جس گواہی سے حق کا ظہور زیادہ قوئی اور واضح ہو اسی پر فیصلہ کرنا واجب ہے لہذا قابض کے گواہوں کی گواہی کے مطابق قابض کے حق میں فیصلہ صادر کیا جائیگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے نتاج اور نکاح مثلا خالد کے قبضہ میں ایک بکری ہے اس پر حامد نے دعوی کیا اور ہر ایک نے بینہ پیش کیا کہ یہ بکری میری ملک میں میری مملوکہ بکری سے پیدا ہوئی ہے تو اس صورت میں قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ایک عورت پر دو مردوں نے نکاح کا دعوی کیا اور یہ عورت ان میں سے ایک کے قبضہ میں ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی قابض کے گواہ قبول ہوتے ہیں۔
اسی طرح اگر شاہد کے قبضہ میں اگر ایک غلام ہو اور اس پر زاہد نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ میرا غلام ہے میں نے اس کو آزاد کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک باندی ایک کے قبضہ میں ہوا اور دوسرے غیر قابض نے دعوی کیا کہ میں نے
The evidence of the possessor is not accepted in absolute ownership, and the evidence of the external claimant is better. Al-Shafi'i said: Judgment is given on the evidence of the possessor because it is strengthened by possession, thus the appearance (of truth) is strengthened, and it becomes like the cases of offspring, marriage, and claims of ownership along with manumission, umm walad, or tadbir. Our evidence is that the evidence of the external claimant is more affirming or more manifest, because what the possession has proven cannot be proven by the evidence of the possessor, since possession is an indication of absolute ownership, unlike offspring, because possession does not indicate it, and likewise for manumission and its two companions, and for the wala' that is established by them. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said that in absolute ownership, the evidence of the possessor is not accepted, and the evidence of the external claimant is better. Imam al-Shafi'i said that judgment is given on the evidence of the possessor because his evidence is strengthened by possession, thus the appearance is strengthened, and it becomes like the cases of offspring and marriage and claims of ownership along with manumission or umm walad. Our evidence is that the evidence of the external claimant is more affirming or more manifest, because what possession has proven is not proven by the evidence of the possessor, since possession is an indication of absolute ownership, unlike offspring, because possession does not indicate it, and likewise for manumission and its two companions, and for the wala' established by them. Explanation: The issue is that if a person is in possession of a specific property and another person claims it, there are two scenarios: one is a restricted claim where the claimant mentions a cause of ownership, e.g., this slave is mine because he was born from my female slave in my ownership. The second is an absolute claim where the claimant does not mention a cause. In the case of absolute ownership, if both the possessor and the external claimant bring evidence, according to us, the external claimant's evidence is better, so it is accepted, and the possessor's evidence is not accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the possessor's witnesses are accepted because his evidence is strengthened by possession, so the appearance of truth is stronger. He gave examples of offspring and marriage where the possessor's evidence is accepted.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri's matn about evidence in cases of competing claims of ownership when one party is in possession (qabid) and the other is not (kharij). The ruling distinguishes between 'absolute ownership' (milk mutlaq) and 'restricted ownership' (milk muqayyad). In absolute ownership, the claimant does not specify a cause; in restricted ownership, he does. The Hanafi position is that in absolute ownership, the possessor's evidence is not accepted because his possession itself already serves as a proof of his ownership. The external claimant's evidence, on the other hand, provides additional proof that outweighs the mere fact of possession. Therefore, the external claimant's evidence is preferred (awla). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that possession strengthens the possessor's evidence, making it more reliable. He analogizes to cases like offspring (natal/nataj) and marriage, where the possessor's evidence is accepted because possession indicates a specific right. For example, if a person is in possession of a sheep and both he and another claim it as their own offspring, the possessor's evidence is accepted because his possession of the sheep supports his claim of ownership from birth. Similarly, in a marriage dispute where both men claim a woman as wife and she is in the possession of one, the possessor's evidence is accepted. The Hanafi rebuttal is that possession is a general indicator of ownership, so it does not need additional evidence; the external claimant's evidence, however, establishes a specific right that overcomes the general indication. The commentary further explains the two scenarios and reiterates that in absolute ownership, the external claimant's evidence is accepted. The text then discusses the Shafi'i view in detail with examples, contrasting with the Hanafi position. The key distinction is that in cases like offspring (natal), possession is not a strong indicator of ownership because the offspring could be from someone else, so the evidence of both is weighed equally. But in absolute ownership, possession is a strong indicator, so the external claimant needs strong evidence to overcome it.

Key Terms
ملک مطلق (milk mutlaq): Absolute ownership claimed without specifying the cause or means of acquisition.
قابض (qabid): The person in actual physical possession of the disputed property.
بينة الخارج (bayyinatu al-kharij): Evidence brought by the claimant who is not in possession.
نتاج (natal): Offspring of an animal; used as example of a restricted ownership claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an absolute ownership claim (milk mutlaq), whose evidence is preferred according to the Hanafi school?
A) The evidence of the possessor (qabid) because he is in possession.
B) The evidence of the external claimant (kharij) because it provides new proof.
C) Both are equal and the judge decides arbitrarily.
D) Neither is accepted until they provide more witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In absolute ownership claims, the external claimant's evidence is preferred because possession alone is a complete proof of ownership.

Preference of External Evidence in Absolute Ownership Disputes
Inter-madhhab dispute on evidence preference in absolute ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on evidence preference in absolute ownership disputes and explain the rationale distinguishing it from specific ownership claims.

Core Idea
In absolute ownership, possession already proves ownership, so external evidence is more probative.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i over whose evidence prevails when two parties claim absolute ownership of property in the hands of one. The Hanafi position, as laid down by al-Quduri, relies on the principle that possession is a strong indicator of ownership in absolute claims, making the possessor's evidence merely confirmatory. Consequently, the external claimant's evidence is given precedence as it establishes ownership anew.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in milk mutlaq: the evidence of the non-possessor (kharij) is preferred over that of the possessor (qabid).
The matn says: 'لا تقبل بينة صاحب اليد فى الملك المطلق وبينة الخارج اولى'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the possessor's evidence should be accepted because possession strengthens it, making his right more manifest.
Al-Shafi'i analogizes to cases of specific causes (milk muqayyad) like offspring or marriage.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas: just as in milk muqayyad the possessor's evidence is preferred due to possession, the same should apply in milk mutlaq.
He cites four cases: natāj (offspring), nikah (marriage), iʿtāq (emancipation), umm walad, tadbir.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes: in milk muqayyad, possession does not indicate the specific cause, so both evidence are equal; in milk mutlaq, possession already indicates ownership, so the possessor's evidence is merely confirmatory.
External evidence establishes original ownership, hence it is more probative.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi court, if both produce evidence in milk mutlaq, the judge rules for the external claimant; in a Shafi'i court, for the possessor.
This difference affects real litigation outcomes.

ملک مطلق میں قابض کے بینہ قبول نہ ہوں گے اور غیر قابض کے بینہ اولی ہیں
قال ولا تقبل بينة صاحب اليد فى الملك المطلق وبينة الخارج اولى وقال الشافعي يقضى ببينة ذى اليد لاعتضادها باليد فيقوى الظهور وصار كالنتاج والنكاح ودعوى الملك مع الاعتاق او الاستيلاد او التدبير ولنا ان بينة الخارج أكثر اثباتا او اظهارا لان قدر ما اثبته اليد لا يثبته بينة ذى اليد اذا اليد دليل مطلق الملك بخلاف النتاج لان اليد لا تدل عليه وكذا على الاعتاق و اختيه [؟] وعلى الولاء الثابت بها
ترجمہ . صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ ملک مطلق میں قابض کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا اور غیر قابض کا بینہ اولی ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قابض کے بینہ پر فیصلہ ہوگا کیونکہ قبضہ کی وجہ سے بعینہ قوی ہو گیا لہذا ظہور بھی قوی ہوگا اور یہ نتائج اور نکاح اور دعوی ملک مع الاعتاق یا مع اللہ بیر کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر قابض کا بینہ زیادہ مثبت یا زیادہ مظہر ہے کیونکہ جس قدر قبضہ نے ثابت کیا ہے قابض کے بعینہ نے اس کا بھی ثابت نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے کہ قبضہ تو مطلق ملک کی دلیل ہے برخلاف آج کے کیونکہ قبضه تا حملات می تابان طرح اعتناق اور استیلا دونہ یہ اور اس ولاء پر جو ان سے ثابت ہوتی ہے بندہ دلالت نہیں مرتاب۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص مال معین پر قابض ہے اور اس پر ایک غیر تیا بعض نے دعوئی کیا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں، ایک تو یہ کہ اس نے ملک مقید کا دعوی کیا یعنی ملک کا دعوی کیا اور مالک ہونے کا سبب بھی ذکر کیا مثلاً یہ کہا کہ یہ غلام جس پر یہ شخص قابض ہے میرا ہے اور میرا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ یہ میری ملک میں میری باندی سے پیدا ہوا ہے یا یہ بیل میرا ہے کیونکہ یہ میری مملوکہ گائے سے میری ملک میں پیدا ہوا ہے۔
-۲۔ دوم یہ کہ اس نے ملک مطلق کا دعوی کیا یعنی ملک کا دعوی تو کیا لیکن مالک ہونے کا سبب بیان نہیں کیا مثلا یہ کہا کہ یہ چیز میری ملک ہے اور اس قابض کے قبضہ میں ناحق طور پر ہے پس ملک مطلق کی صورت میں اگر قابض نے اپنے مالک ہونے پر بینہ پیش کیا اور غیر قابض نے اپنے مالک ہونے پر بینہ پیش کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک غیر قابض کا بینہ اولی ہوگا لہذا وہی قبول ہوگا اور غیر تقابض کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر قابض کا بینہ اس کے واسطے ملک ثابت کرتا ہے اور قابض کا بینہ، قابض کے واسطے ملک ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے کیونکہ قابض کی ملک اس کے قبضہ سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے پس قابض کا بینہ اس کے واسطے مڑکر ہو گا جو ملک سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور تاکید ، موجود کے لئے وصف کو ثابت کرنے کا نام ہے۔ نہ کہ اصل ملک کو ثابت کرنے کا نام۔ بہر حال جب قابض کا بینہ ثابت شدہ ملک کے لئے مؤکد ہے اور غیر قابض کا بینہ سے ملک کا اثبات یا اظہار زیادہ ہے تو قابض کے قبضہ کی وجہ سے ظاہری ملک پر غیر قابض کے بینہ کو ترجیح ہوگی اور ایس ترجیح کی وجہ سے اس کا بینہ قبول ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف نتاج کہ اس پر قبضہ دلالت نہیں کرتا ہے اس طرح اعتناق ، استیلا داور تدبیر اور وہ ولاء جوان سے ثابت ہے ان پر قبضہ دلالت نہیں کرتا ہے بلکہ قبضہ سے صرف ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے اور نتاج وغیرہ قبضہ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتے حاصل یہ کہ نتاج وغیرہ کو قابض اور غیر قابض دونوں کے گواہوں نے یکساں طور پر ثابت کیا ہے۔ لہذا اب ترجیح کی ضرورت پیش آئی تو ہم نے قابض کے گواہوں کو اس کے قبضہ کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی اور ملک مقید کی صورت میں قابض کے گواہوں کو قبول کرنے کا فیصلہ کیا۔
In absolute ownership, the evidence of the possessor is not accepted, and the evidence of the external person is more deserving. Imam Shafi'i said: Judgment is given based on the evidence of the possessor because it is strengthened by possession, so the appearance is strengthened, and it becomes like offspring, marriage, claim of ownership along with emancipation or making umm walad or tadbir. Our proof is that the evidence of the external person is more establishing or more manifest, because what possession establishes is not established by the evidence of the possessor, since possession is evidence of absolute ownership, unlike offspring because possession does not indicate it, and similarly emancipation, making umm walad, tadbir, and the wala established by them.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Da'wa addresses a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whose evidence (bayyinah) is preferred when two parties claim ownership of a property in the possession of one of them. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: in cases of absolute ownership (al-milk al-mutlaq) where the claimant does not specify a cause of ownership, the evidence of the non-possessor (al-kharij) is preferable and thus accepted over that of the possessor (sahib al-yad). Imam al-Shafi'i opposes this, arguing that the possessor's evidence is strengthened by the fact of possession, making his claim appear stronger, similar to cases of specific causes like offspring (natāj), marriage (nikah), or claims of ownership with emancipation (iʿtāq), making umm walad, or tadbir. The Hanafi response is that external evidence is more probative because possession itself already establishes a prima facie case of ownership for the possessor; thus his evidence merely reinforces what is already indicated by possession, whereas the external evidence establishes ownership anew. In contrast, in cases of specific causes (milk muqayyad), possession does not indicate those specific causes, so both parties' evidence is equal and the possessor's evidence is preferred due to his possession. The commentary then elaborates with examples: if both parties claim the animal was born from their own livestock, or if two men claim marriage to a woman in one's possession, the possessor's evidence prevails. Similarly, if the possessor claims emancipation, umm walad, or tadbir, his evidence is accepted. However, in absolute ownership, the external evidence is preferred.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, presented in court to prove a claim.
ملك مطلق (milk mutlaq): Ownership claimed without specifying the cause or mode of acquisition (e.g., purchase, inheritance).
قابض (qabid): The person who is in physical possession of the disputed property.
خارج (kharij): The person who is not in possession; the external claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In absolute ownership, the external claimant's evidence is preferred because the possessor's possession already indicates ownership, making his evidence merely confirmatory.

Judgment by Refusal of Oath (Nukul) – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on the effect of nukul (refusal of oath) in litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on nukul (defendant's refusal of oath), contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and identify the basis of each school's argument.

Core Idea
A defendant's refusal to swear is proof enough for a Hanafi judge to rule against him.

In a dispute where the defendant has no evidence and is asked to swear, what happens if he refuses? The Hanafi school treats this refusal as a form of admission, leading to an immediate judgment. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that refusal is ambiguous and the oath should be returned to the plaintiff. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both views and the practical consequences for a judge.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the text: When the defendant refuses the oath, the judge rules against him immediately and makes him liable for the claim.
This is the position of al-Quduri's matn.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the judge does not rule against the defendant based on refusal alone; instead, the oath is returned to the plaintiff, and if he swears, judgment is for the plaintiff.
The Shafi'i view is mentioned to highlight the ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Analyze the Shafi'i reasoning: Refusal could be due to caution against false oath or abstention from a truthful one, making it ambiguous. The plaintiff's oath is clearer evidence.
Note the word 'ihtimal' (probability) – Shafi'i considers refusal as probabilistic, not certain.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that refusal indicates the defendant is either ready to pay or is admitting, because a truthful person would swear to protect himself. This rational inference preponderates over ambiguity.
The Hanafi position relies on 'ghalabat al-zann' (preponderant probability) and treats refusal as a form of iqrar (admission).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a Hanafi court, judgment is immediate upon refusal; in a Shafi'i court, the plaintiff is asked to swear. This affects the burden of proof and the final outcome.
This shows how usul differences affect real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدعی علیہ قسم سے انکار کر دے تو اس کے خلاف قاضی فیصلہ دیدے
قال واذا نكل المدعى عليه عن اليمين قضى عليه بالنكول والزمه ما ادعى عليه وقال الشافعي لا يقضى به بل يرد اليمين على المدعى فاذا حلف يقضى به لان النكول يحتمل التورع عن اليمين الكاذبة والترفع عن الصادقة واشتباه الحال فلا ينتصب حجة مع الاحتمال ويمين المدعى دليل الظهور فيصار اليه ولنا ان النكول دل على كونه باذلا او مقرا اذ لو لا ذالك لاقدم على اليمين اقامة للواجب ودفعا للضرر عن نفسه فيترجح هذا الجانب ولا وجه لرد اليمين عـلـى الـمـدعــى لــمــا قــدمـنـاه
ترجمہ اور جب مدعی علیہ نے قسم سے نکار کیا تو قاضی انکار کی وجہ سے اس کے خلاف فیصلہ کرے گا اور جو کچھ مدعی نے اس پر دعوی کیا ہے وہ اس کے ذمہ لازم کرے گا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی انکار کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ پر حکم نہ دے گا بلکہ قسم کو مدعی پر لوٹائے گا پس اگر مدعی قسم کھا گیا تو قاضی اس کے واسطے حکم دیدے گا کیونکہ مدعی علیہ کا قسم سے انکار کرنا اس بات کا احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ جھوٹی قسم سے پر ہیز کرنا چاہتا ہے اور کچی قسم ہے احتیاط کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ (بہر حال ) مدعی علیہ کا انکار اشتباہ حال کا احتمال رکھتا ہے لہذا یہ انکا ر اس احتمال کے ساتھ حجت نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور مدعی کا قسم کھانا ظہور حق کی دلیل ہے۔ لہذا اسی کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے مدعی علیہ کا قسم سے انکار اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ مدعی بہ کو دلیری کے ساتھ دینا چاہتا ہے یا وہ مدعی
If the defendant refuses to take the oath, the judge rules against him due to his refusal and makes him liable for what was claimed. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He does not rule against him, but returns the oath to the plaintiff. If the plaintiff swears, then he rules for him. Because refusal may be due to caution against a false oath or abstention from a truthful one, and the situation is ambiguous, so it cannot be a proof with probability. The plaintiff's oath is evidence of the right's appearance, so it is resorted to. Our proof is that the refusal indicates that he is willing to pay or is admitting, because otherwise he would proceed with the oath to fulfill the obligation and repel harm from himself, so this side is preponderant. There is no basis to return the oath to the plaintiff as we have presented.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal effect of a defendant's refusal to take an oath (al-nukul 'an al-yamin). The Hanafi position, attributed to al-Quduri, is that when the defendant refuses to swear after being required to do so, the judge immediately rules against him, holding him liable for the claim. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, holds that the judge does not rule against the defendant based on refusal alone; instead, the oath is returned to the plaintiff, and if the plaintiff swears, judgment is given in his favor. The Shafi'i argument is that refusal can be interpreted in multiple ways—perhaps the defendant is avoiding a false oath or even refraining from a truthful one out of piety—so it is ambiguous and cannot serve as conclusive proof. The oath of the plaintiff, however, directly manifests the right. The Hanafi counterargument is that refusal is strong evidence that the defendant is either ready to surrender the claim or is tacitly admitting it, because if he were truthful, he would overcome any scruples and take the oath to protect his own interest and fulfill the religious obligation (if the oath is not sinful). Thus, the refusal is taken as an admission (iqrar), and judgment is entered accordingly. The Hanafi school relies on the principle that necessity (defending oneself against false claims) would compel a truthful defendant to swear, so refusal indicates lack of truthfulness.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath when required by the judge.
يمين (yamin): Oath sworn by a party in litigation, typically invoked when one party lacks evidence.
مدعى عليه (mudda'a alayh): The defendant against whom a claim is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi court, if the defendant refuses to take the oath after being required, what happens?
A) The case is dismissed
B) The judge rules against the defendant immediately
C) The oath is given to the plaintiff
D) The defendant is imprisoned until he swears

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge considers a defendant's refusal to take an oath as sufficient proof to rule against him, because a truthful person would swear to protect himself.

Priority of Possessor's Evidence in Ownership Disputes
Explaining Hanafi ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the possessor's evidence is accepted over the non-possessor's, explain the proof based on possession indicating ownership, and apply the qiyas from restricted to unrestricted ownership.

Core Idea
Possession proves ownership, so the possessor's evidence is confirmatory, not foundational.

In Hanafi fiqh, when both a possessor and a non-possessor claim ownership of property and each presents evidence, the court must decide which evidence to accept. This passage explains the ruling: the possessor's evidence is given priority. The reasoning is that possession itself already indicates ownership, so the possessor's evidence merely confirms what is already established. The non-possessor's evidence, by contrast, would establish new ownership, which is weaker. The ruling is extended by qiyas from restricted ownership (like umm walad or tadbir) to unrestricted ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
In the passage, there is a possessor (qabid) who has possession of a slave or slave girl and claims a restricted ownership attribute (e.g., umm walad or mudabbar). A non-possessor claims absolute ownership (milk mutlaq) over the same property. Both present evidence (bayyinah).
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the possessor's evidence is accepted over the non-possessor's. This applies to both restricted ownership (milk muqayyad) and, by analogy, unrestricted ownership (milk mutlaq).
The passage explicitly extends the ruling from restricted to unrestricted.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is that the non-possessor's evidence establishes ownership, while the possessor's evidence does not; it merely confirms ownership already proven by possession. Possession (qabd) indicates ownership, so the possessor's evidence is corroborative (tākīd), not foundational.
This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the nature of possession.
4
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is first established for restricted ownership (e.g., umm walad, tadbir). The 'illa (effective cause) is that possession indicates ownership. Since this 'illa is present in unrestricted ownership as well, the ruling is applied analogically.
The qiyas is jali (clear) because the 'illa is obvious.
5
Note the exception for offspring
The passage clarifies that for offspring (natāj) or other attributes not indicated by possession (like acquisition, control, tadbir, wala'), both parties' witnesses are equal. However, preference is still given to the possessor due to his possession.
Possession does not indicate birthing status, so the evidence is balanced, but possession tips the scale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس باندی کو اپنی ملک میں لا کرام ولد بنایا ہے اور اس پر بینہ قائم کر دیا اور قابض نے کہا کہ میں نے اس کو ام ولد بنایا ہے اور اس پر بینہ قائم کر دیا تو اس صورت میں بھی قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوتا ہے اس طرح اگر ایک شخص کے قبضہ میں ایک غلام ہے اور اس نے دعوی کیا ہو کہ میں نے اس کو مد بر بنایا ہے اور اس پر بینہ قائم کر دیا اور ایک غیر قابض آدمی نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ غلام میرا ہے میں نے اس کو مد بر بنایا ہے اور اس پر بینہ قائم کر دیا۔ تو قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوگا پس جس طرح ان مسائل میں یعنی ملک مقید میں قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ملک مطلق میں قابض کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر قابض کا بینہ اس کے واسطے ملک ثابت کرتا ہے اور قابض کا بینہ، قابض کے واسطے ملک ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے کیونکہ قابض کی ملک اس کے قبضہ سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے پس قابض کا بینہ اس کے واسطے مڑکر ہو گا جو ملک سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور تاکید ، موجود کے لئے وصف کو ثابت کرنے کا نام ہے۔ نہ کہ اصل ملک کو ثابت کرنے کا نام۔ بہر حال جب قابض کا بینہ ثابت شدہ ملک کے لئے مؤکد ہے اور غیر قابض کا بینہ سے ملک کا اثبات یا اظہار زیادہ ہے تو قابض کے قبضہ کی وجہ سے ظاہری ملک پر غیر قابض کے بینہ کو ترجیح ہوگی اور ایس ترجیح کی وجہ سے اس کا بینہ قبول ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف نتاج کہ اس پر قبضہ دلالت نہیں کرتا ہے اس طرح اعتناق ، استیلا داور تدبیر اور وہ ولاء جوان سے ثابت ہے ان پر قبضہ دلالت نہیں کرتا ہے بلکہ قبضہ سے صرف ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے اور نتاج وغیرہ قبضہ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتے حاصل یہ کہ نتاج وغیرہ کو قابض اور غیر قابض دونوں کے گواہوں نے یکساں طور پر ثابت کیا ہے۔ لہذا اب ترجیح کی ضرورت پیش آئی تو ہم نے قابض کے گواہوں کو اس کے قبضہ کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی اور ملک مقید کی صورت میں قابض کے گواہوں کو قبول کرنے کا فیصلہ کیا۔
He has brought this slave girl into his possession and made her (something) and established evidence upon that, and the possessor said: 'I have made her umm walad' and established evidence upon that, then in this case also the possessor's evidence is accepted. Similarly, if a slave is in the possession of a person and he claimed that he made him mudabbar and established evidence, and a non-possessor claimed that this slave is mine, I made him mudabbar and established evidence, then the possessor's evidence will be accepted. So just as in these cases of restricted ownership the possessor's evidence is accepted, similarly in unrestricted ownership the possessor's evidence will be accepted. Our proof is that the non-possessor's evidence establishes ownership for him, whereas the possessor's evidence does not establish ownership for the possessor because the possessor's ownership is established by his possession. Thus the possessor's evidence becomes a corroboration for what is established by ownership, and corroboration is to prove an attribute for an existing thing, not to prove original ownership. In any case, when the possessor's evidence is corroborative for established ownership, and the non-possessor's evidence gives more establishment or manifestation of ownership, then due to the possessor's possession preference is given to the non-possessor's evidence over the apparent ownership, and due to this preference his evidence will be accepted. Contrary to offspring, possession does not indicate that; similarly, acquisition, control, tadbir, and wala' established from it, possession does not indicate these; rather, possession only establishes ownership, and offspring etc. are not established by possession. The conclusion is that offspring etc. are equally proved by the witnesses of both possessor and non-possessor. Hence, the need for preference arose, so we have given preference to the possessor's witnesses due to his possession and decided to accept the possessor's witnesses in the case of restricted ownership.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the priority of evidence in ownership disputes. The ruling states that when both a possessor (qabid) and a non-possessor (ghayr qabid) present evidence claiming ownership (with specific attributes like umm walad or mudabbar), the possessor's evidence is accepted. This is because the possessor's possession already indicates ownership, so his evidence is merely confirmatory (tākīd), whereas the non-possessor's evidence would establish new ownership. The proof uses qiyas (analogy) from cases of restricted ownership (milk muqayyad) to unrestricted ownership (milk mutlaq). The commentator then explains that for things like offspring (natāj) or other attributes that are not indicated by possession, both parties' evidence is equal, but preference is given to the possessor because of his possession. The Hanafi position is that the possessor's evidence is accepted due to istihsan (juristic preference).

Key Terms
قابض (qābiḍ): The person who has physical possession of the property (slave or slave girl) in dispute.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two witnesses, presented in court to prove a claim.
ملک مقید (milk muqayyad): Ownership with a specific restriction or attribute, such as being umm walad or mudabbar.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave concubine who has borne a child to her master, who becomes free upon her master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom by his master, effective after the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The court asks the slave to testify
D) The case is dismissed due to equal evidence

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the possessor's evidence is accepted over the non-possessor's because possession itself proves ownership, making the possessor's evidence confirmatory.
