Taking Surety on Mere Claim: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Explains the Hanafi ruling on compelling surety for a defendant's appearance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking surety for a defendant on a mere claim, explain the istihsan argument, and identify the conditions for compelling surety.

Core Idea
Istihsan allows taking a surety on mere claim because the defendant must attend anyway, and it protects the plaintiff without harming the defendant.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) where Al-Marghinani explains that taking a surety for the defendant's personal appearance is permitted by istihsan even though mere claim does not establish a right. The ruling balances the plaintiff's need to secure his right with the defendant's obligation to attend court, and sets out conditions such as the plaintiff having witnesses present in the city.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that kafalah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person) is valid, and compelling a surety on mere claim is permitted by istihsan under certain conditions.
The ruling is based on istihsan, which overrides the qiyas that would otherwise prohibit it.
2
Understand the opposing qiyas
Recognize the qiyas argument: a mere claim does not establish entitlement, so requiring a surety is unjustified. This view is held by Qatada and Imam Sha'bi.
This qiyas is the default analogy that the Hanafi school sets aside via istihsan.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Examine the reasoning: attendance is due from the defendant on mere claim (the judge can compel attendance), so taking a surety to ensure that attendance is a valid means; it benefits the plaintiff and does not harm the defendant.
The key point: since attendance is already wajib, a surety is a reasonable precaution.
4
Note the conditions
Identify that the plaintiff must state he has witnesses present in the city (bayyina hadira). If he has no witnesses or they are absent, no surety is taken due to lack of benefit.
Also note the exception for a traveler: surety only for the duration of the session.
5
Recognize intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand the differences: Abu Hanifa says three days; Abu Yusuf says until next session; Imam Muhammad exempts well-known persons unlikely to abscond. The mufta bihi is the three-day rule with no distinction based on status.
The commentator explicitly states that three days is sahih and the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwayah) makes no distinction.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الدَّعْوَىٰ
اشرف الہدایہ جلد وہم حقه والكفالة بالنفس جائزة عندنا وقد مر من قبل واخذ الكفيل بمجرد الدعوى استحسان عندنا لان فيه نظراً للمدعى وليس فيه كثير ضرر بالمدعى عليه ولهذا لان الحضور مستحق عليه بمجرد الدعوى حتى يعدى عليه ويحال بينه وبين اشغاله فيصح التكفيل باحضاره والتقدير بثلثة ايام مروى عن ابي حنيفة وهو الصحيح ولافرق فى الظاهر بين الخامل والوجية والحقير من المال والخطير ثم لا بد من قوله لى بينة حاضرة التكفيل ومعناه في المصر حتى لو قال المدعى لابينة لى او شهودى غيب لا يكفل لعدم الفائدة . قال فان فعل والا امر بملازمته كيلا يذهب حقه الا ان يكون غريبا فيلا زم مقدار مجلس القاضى وكذا لا يكفل الا الى اخر المجلس فالاستثناء منصرف اليهما لان فى اخذ الكفيل والملازمة زيادة على ذالك اضرار به يمنعه عن السفر ولا ضرر فى هذا المقدار ظاهرا وكيفية الملازمة نذكرها في كتاب الحجر ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ اگر مدعی نے کہا کہ میرے گواہ شہر میں موجود ہیں تو اس کے مدنی علیہ سے کہا جائے گا کہ تو تین دن کے واسطے اس کو اپنی ذات کا کفیل دے تا کہ مدنی علیہ روپوش نہ ہو جائے کہ مدعی کا حق ضائع ہو جائے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک کفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے اور یہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے اور محض دعوی پر کفیل لینا ہمارے نزدیک استحسانا جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں مدعی کے واسطے بھلائی ہے اور اس میں مدعی علیہ کے واسطے زیادہ ضر نہیں ہے اور یہ اس لئے محض دعوی سے مدعی علیہ پر حاضر ہونا واجب ہے حتی کہ مدعی علیہ کی حاضری پر حاکم سے مدد لی جاتی ہے اور مدعی علیہ اور اس کے کاموں کے درمیان حیلوت کر دی جاتی ہے پس اس کی حاضری پر کفیل لینا جائز ہے اور تین دن کے ساتھ اندازہ کرنا ابوحنیفہ کی روایت ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق بے قدراور وجیہ آدمی اور حقیر مال اور کثیر مال کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔
پھر کفالت کے واسطے مدعی کا قول الى بينة حاضرة ضروری ہے اور اس کے معنی ہیں شہر میں حتی کہ اگر مدعی نے کہا کہ میرے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے یا میرے گواہ غائب ہیں تو کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا کیونکہ کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے پس اگر مدعلی علیہ نے کفیل دیدیا تو فبہا ور نہ تو مدعی کو اس کے ساتھ ساتھ رہنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا تا کہ اس کا حق ضائع نہ ہو مگر یہ کہ مدعی علیہ پر دیہی آدمی ہو تو مدعی مجلس قاضی کی مقدار اس کے ساتھ لگارہے گا اور اسی طرح اس مسافر سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا مگر قاضی کی آخر مجلس تک پس استثناء دونوں کی طرف راجع ہے اس لئے کہ اس مقدار سے زیادہ کے لئے کفیل لینا اور مدعی علیہ کے دامن گیر ہونا ایسا ضرور ہے جو اس کو سفر سے روکتا ہے اور اس مقدار میں بظاہر کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے اور ساتھ ساتھ رہنے کی کیفیت کو ہم ان شاء اللہ کتاب الحجر میں ذکر کر رہیں گے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مدعی نے مجلس قاضی میں کہا کہ میرے گواہ شہر میں موجود ہیں تو اسکے بدی عالیہ کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ تین دن کے واسطے اپنی ذات کا کفیل دیدے یعنی کوئی شخص مدعی علیہ کی حاضری کا ضامن ہونا چاہئے ۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ اگر مدعی علیہ سے کفیل نہ لیا گیا تو مدعی علیہ روپوش ہو سکتا ہے اور مدلی علیہ کے روپوش ہونے کی صورت میں مدعی کا حق ضائع ہو سکتا ہے پس مدعی کے حق کو ضائع ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے مولی علیہ کونفیل دینے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور کفالہ بالنفس اگر چہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے لیکن ہمارے نزدیک حکم جائز ہے اس کی تفصیل کتاب الکفالہ کے اول میں گذر چکی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مدعی نے اگر صرف دعوی کیاور بینہ پیش نہ کر سکا تو صرف دعوی کی بنیاد پر مدنی علیہ سے کفیل لینا جائز نہیں ہے یہی قتادہ اور امام شعبی سے مروی ہے اور استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدنی علیہ سے کفیل لینا جائز ہے یہی ہمارے علماء کا مذہب ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کر محض دعوی استحقاق کا سبب نہیں ہے یعنی محض دعوئی سے مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کا حق ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے اور محض دعوی استحقاق کا سبب کیسے ہوگا حالانکہ مدعی علیہ کا انکار مدعی کے دعوی کے معارض ہے۔ بہر حال جب محض دعوی سے مدعی علیہ پر کوئی حق ثابت نہیں ہوا تو مدعی علیہ کفیل کا دینا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ سے کفیل لینے میں مدعی پر شفقت ہے اس طور پر کہ کفیل دینے کے بعد مدعی علیہ بھاگ نہیں سکے گا اور جب مدعی علیہ بھاگ نہیں سکے گا تو مدعی اس کے خلاف بینہ قائم کرنے پر قادر ہو سکے گا بہر حال اس میں مدعی کا فائدہ ہے اور مدعلی علیہ کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے اور مدعی علیہ کا نقصان اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ محض دعوی پر مدعی علیہ کے ذمہ حاضر ہونا واجب ہے حتی کہ مدعلی علیہ کی حاضری پر جا کم سے مدد لی جاتی ہے اور مدعی علیہ کو اس کے کاموں سے روک دیا جاتا ہے پس جب محض دعوی پر مدعی علیہ کی حاضری ضروری ہے تو اس کی حاضری پر کفیل اور ضامن لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ عبارت میں بعدی ، مضارع مجہول اعداء سے ماخوذ ہے جس کے معنی مدد طلب کرنے کے ہیں اسی سے شاعر کا قول ہے۔
ونستدعى الاميرا ذا ظلمنا ومن يعدى الظلم الامير جب ہم پر کوئی ظلم کرتا ہے تو ہم امیر سے مدد طلب کرتے ہیں لیکن جب امیر ہی ظالم ہو تو کس سے مدد طلب کی جائے گی ۔ شعر میں اعداء اور استعداء دونوں مدد طلب کرنے کے معنی میں مستعمل ہیں۔ اس مضمون کو ایک اردو کے شاعر نے اس طرح پیش کیا ہے : وہی قاتل وہی منصف وہی حاکم ٹھہرے اقرباء میرے کریں خون کا دعوی کس پر
ایک اور شاعر نے کہا ہے:
ہم نے سوچا تھا کہ حاکم سے کریں گے فریاد وہ بھی کمبخت تیرا چاہنے والا نکالا صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کفیل لینے کے سلسلہ میں تین دن کی تحدید حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی روایت ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور نہ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کی دوسری مجلس منعقد ہونے تک مدعی علیہ سے کفیل لیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق وجیہ اور غیر وجیہ آدمی کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے یعنی مدعی علیہ وجیہ ہو یا غیر وجیہہ آدمی اور مال دعوای حقیر ہو یا کثیر ہو بہر صورت مدعی علیہ کو فیل دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ حضرت امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ مدعی علیہ اگر زی و جاہت آدمی ہو اور ایسا معروف و مشہور ہو کہ بظاہر وہ اپنے آپ کو روپوش نہیں کرے گا تو ایسی صورت میں مدعلی علیہ کو فیل دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ کفالہ کیلئے دی کا یہ کہنا ضروری ہے کہ میرے گواہ شہر میں موجود ہیں حتی کہ اگر ندی نے کہا کہ میرے پاس گواہ نہیں ہیں یا میرے گواہ غائب ہیں تو اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں کفیل لینے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ کفالہ کا فائدہ تو یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کے عاجز ہونے پر کفیل مدعی علیہ کو حاضر کز دے لیکن جب گواہ ہی موجود نہیں ہیں تو مد علی علیہ کو کیسے حاضر کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Claims. Kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible according to us and has been mentioned before. Taking a surety on mere claim is istihsan according to us because it considers the plaintiff and there is not much harm to the defendant. Attendance is due from him on mere claim so that he is sought help against and prevented from his work. So taking a surety for his attendance is valid. The estimation of three days is narrated from Abu Hanifa and it is the correct view. In the apparent (zāhir al-riwāyah) there is no difference between the obscure and the respected, nor between insignificant and significant property. Then the plaintiff must say 'I have witnesses present' for kafālah, meaning in the city. If the plaintiff says 'I have no evidence' or 'my witnesses are absent', no surety is taken due to lack of benefit. He said: if he does that, otherwise he is ordered to accompany him so his right is not lost, unless he is a traveler; then he accompanies for the duration of the judge's session. Likewise, surety is not taken except until the end of the session. The exception refers to both because taking surety and accompaniment beyond that harms him by preventing travel, but in this amount there is no apparent harm. The manner of accompaniment we will mention in Kitab al-Hajr, God willing. 
[Translation of Urdu commentary follows the same meaning: explaining that if plaintiff says witnesses are in town, defendant must give a surety for three days; kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible in our school; the rationale is to protect plaintiff's right while not harming defendant; the condition that plaintiff states he has witnesses present; the exception for traveler; the dispute about three days vs. next session; Imam Muhammad's view about well-known person; etc.]
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the ruling on taking a surety (kafīl) for the defendant's personal appearance in a lawsuit. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: kafālah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person) is valid, as previously established. Taking a surety from the defendant merely upon the plaintiff's claim (without proof) is permitted by istihān (juristic preference). The reasoning is that this protects the plaintiff's interest (nazar li'l-mudda'ī) while causing no substantial harm to the defendant, because the defendant is already obliged to attend court by virtue of the mere claim; the judge can compel attendance and even prevent him from his work. Since attendance is due, taking a surety to ensure it is valid. The time limit for the surety is three days, narrated from Abu Hanifa and considered the correct view. According to the apparent transmission (zāhir al-riwāyah), there is no distinction between a lowly person (khāmil) and a respected one (wajīh), nor between a small or large claim. The condition for compelling the surety is that the plaintiff must state, 'I have witnesses present in the city.' If the plaintiff has no witnesses or they are absent, no surety is taken because there is no benefit. If the defendant provides a surety, it is accepted; otherwise, the court orders the plaintiff to accompany the defendant (mulāzama) to prevent the right from being lost. However, if the defendant is a traveler (gharīb), he is only required to be accompanied for the duration of the judge's session, and no surety is taken except until the end of the session. The exception for the traveler applies to both surety and accompaniment, because requiring more would harm him by preventing travel. The details of mulāzama will be covered in Kitab al-Hajr. The commentary then elaborates on the rationale, including a comparison with Qatada and Sha'bi who opposed taking surety on mere claim, and clarifies that the Hanafi school follows istihān. It also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the surety lasts until the next court session, while Imam Muhammad holds that a well-known person (dhī wajāha) who is unlikely to abscond should not be compelled to give a surety.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafālah bi al-nafs): Suretyship for the person of the defendant, guaranteeing his presence in court.
مستحسن (istihān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason (benefit, necessity).
بينة حاضرة (bayyina hādira): Witnesses present in the city at the time of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition that must be stated by the plaintiff for the court to compel the defendant to provide a surety for his appearance?
A) The plaintiff must show written evidence of his claim.
B) The plaintiff must state that he has witnesses present in the city.
C) The defendant must admit the claim.
D) The claim must involve a large amount of property.

Key Takeaway
Taking a surety on mere claim is permissible by istihsan when the plaintiff has witnesses present, and the surety is for three days with no distinction of status.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Taking a Surety from the Defendant Without Evidence: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Presents two views on taking a surety without evidence, adopting Hanafi istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking a surety from a defendant without evidence and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits what qiyas forbids: a surety without evidence to protect the plaintiff.

In the Hanafi school, judicial procedure often balances strict analogy with practical fairness. This passage from Kitab al-Da'wa presents a clear example: should a plaintiff without evidence be allowed to take a surety from the defendant? The answer hinges on whether we follow qiyas (analogy) or istihsan (juristic preference). Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage addresses whether a plaintiff who has only made a claim (without presenting evidence) can demand a surety (kafil) from the defendant to ensure his appearance in court.
The issue arises because a mere claim does not establish a right.
2
State the opposing view and its proof
Qatada and Imam al-Sha'bi hold that taking a surety is not permissible. Their proof is qiyas: a mere claim is not a cause of entitlement, as the defendant's denial contradicts the claim, so no right is established. Therefore, the defendant cannot be compelled to provide a surety.
3
State the Hanafi view and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that taking a surety is permissible. The proof is istihsan: there is a benefit to the plaintiff (preventing the defendant from fleeing) without harm to the defendant (who is already obligated to appear in court).
Istihsan sets aside qiyas due to this consideration of benefit.
4
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The passage explains that even without a surety, the defendant is obligated to appear based on the mere claim; the court can seek assistance to enforce attendance. Requiring a surety is merely an extension of this existing obligation, so it does not harm the defendant.
The key is that the defendant's obligation to appear is already established by the claim itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position (permissibility by istihsan) is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the school. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts this view, and it is part of the zahir al-riwayah.
This ruling is operative for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

كتاب الدعوى
اشرف الہدایہ جلد و همر
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مدعی نے اگر صرف دعوی کیااور بینہ پیش نہ کر سکا تو صرف دعوی کی بنیاد پر مدنی علیہ سے کفیل لینا جائز نہیں ہے یہی قتادہ اور امام شعبی سے مروی ہے اور استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدنی علیہ سے کفیل لینا جائز ہے یہی ہمارے علماء کا مذہب ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کر محض دعوی استحقاق کا سبب نہیں ہے یعنی محض دعوئی سے مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کا حق ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے اور محض دعوی استحقاق کا سبب کیسے ہوگا حالانکہ مدعی علیہ کا انکار مدعی کے دعوی کے معارض ہے۔ بہر حال جب محض دعوی سے مدعی علیہ پر کوئی حق ثابت نہیں ہوا تو مدعی علیہ کفیل کا دینا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ سے کفیل لینے میں مدعی پر شفقت ہے اس طور پر کہ کفیل دینے کے بعد مدعی علیہ بھاگ نہیں سکے گا اور جب مدعی علیہ بھاگ نہیں سکے گا تو مدعی اس کے خلاف بینہ قائم کرنے پر قادر ہو سکے گا بہر حال اس میں مدعی کا فائدہ ہے اور مدعلی علیہ کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے اور مدعی علیہ کا نقصان اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ محض دعوی پر مدعی علیہ کے ذمہ حاضر ہونا واجب ہے حتی کہ مدعلی علیہ کی حاضری پر جا کم سے مدد لی جاتی ہے اور مدعی علیہ کو اس کے کاموں سے روک دیا جاتا ہے پس جب محض دعوی پر مدعی علیہ کی حاضری ضروری ہے تو اس کی حاضری پر کفیل اور ضامن لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ عبارت میں بعدی ، مضارع مجهول اعداء سے ماخوذ ہے جس کے معنی مدد طلب کرنے کے ہیں اسی سے شاعر کا قول ہے۔
ونستدعى الاميرا ذا ظلمنا ومن يعدى الظلم الامير جب ہم پر کوئی ظلم کرتا ہے تو ہم امیر سے مدد طلب کرتے ہیں لیکن جب امیر ہی ظالم ہو تو کس سے مدد طلب کی جائے گی ۔ شعر میں اعداء اور استعداء دونوں مدد طلب کرنے کے معنی میں مستعمل ہیں۔ اس مضمون کو ایک اردو کے شاعر نے اس طرح پیش کیا ہے : وہی قاتل وہی منصف وہی حاکم ٹھہرے اقرباء میرے کریں خون کا دعوی کس پر
ایک اور شاعر نے کہا ہے:
ہم نے سوچا تھا کہ حاکم سے کریں گے فریاد وہ بھی کمبخت تیرا چاہنے والا نکالا
The Book of Claims. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume 10, page 341. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the plaintiff only made a claim and could not present evidence, then taking a surety from the defendant based solely on the claim is not permissible. This is narrated from Qatada and Imam al-Sha'bi. And istihsan is that taking a surety from the defendant is permissible; this is the school of our scholars. The reason for qiyas is that a mere claim is not a cause of entitlement, meaning the plaintiff's right is not established against the defendant by mere claim. And how can a mere claim be a cause of entitlement when the defendant's denial contradicts the plaintiff's claim? In any case, when no right is established against the defendant by mere claim, then the defendant is not obligated to give a surety. And the reason for istihsan is that taking a surety from the defendant is a kindness to the plaintiff, in that after giving a surety, the defendant cannot flee, and when the defendant cannot flee, the plaintiff can establish evidence against him. In any case, this benefits the plaintiff and causes no harm to the defendant. And the defendant is not harmed because by mere claim the defendant is obligated to appear; indeed, for the defendant's appearance, assistance is sought from the authorities, and the defendant is prevented from his work. So when the defendant's appearance is necessary due to mere claim, then taking a surety and guarantor for his appearance is also permissible. In the phrase, 'y'ada' is a passive imperfect derived from 'a'daa' meaning to seek help. From this, the poet said: 'We seek help from the amir when we are wronged, and who will help against the amir's wrongdoing?' In poetry, both 'a'daa' and 'isti'daa' are used in the meaning of seeking help. An Urdu poet presented this idea as: 'He is the killer, he is the judge, he is the ruler; my relatives claim blood-money; against whom?' Another poet said: 'We thought we would complain to the ruler; he too, the wretched one, turned out to be your lover.'
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from Kitab al-Da'wa (Book of Claims) in Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author presents two opposing views on whether a plaintiff can demand a surety (kafil) from the defendant when the plaintiff has no evidence to support his claim. The first view, attributed to Qatada and Imam al-Sha'bi, holds that it is not permissible. Their reasoning is based on qiyas: a mere claim does not establish any right against the defendant, since the defendant's denial contradicts the claim. Therefore, the defendant cannot be compelled to give a surety. The second view, which is the Hanafi school's position and based on istihsan, holds that it is permissible. The Hanafi reasoning is that taking a surety benefits the plaintiff without harming the defendant. The benefit is that the defendant cannot flee, allowing the plaintiff time to bring evidence. The defendant is not harmed because even without a surety, he is obligated to appear in court due to the claim; authorities can compel his attendance and restrict his activities. Thus, requiring a surety is merely an extension of this existing obligation. The passage then includes a linguistic note on the word 'y'ada' (from 'a'daa' meaning to seek help) and two poetic examples illustrating the concept of seeking help from rulers. This is typical in classical commentaries to clarify language and provide cultural context.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): A surety who guarantees the presence of the defendant in court.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; setting aside qiyas for a stronger consideration of benefit.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying the rule of a primary case to a new case based on shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking a surety from the defendant when the plaintiff has no evidence?
A) It is not permissible
B) It is permissible by qiyas
C) It is permissible by istihsan
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits taking a surety from the defendant without evidence through istihsan, prioritizing practical benefit over strict analogy.

Time Limit for Kafala and Wajih Exemption
Intra-Hanafi dispute on surety duration and wajih exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the duration of kafala and explain whether a wajih defendant is exempted from providing a surety according to the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa’s three-day surety limit stands; no exemption for wajih in Zahir al-Riwayah.

In judicial proceedings, a court may require a defendant to provide a surety (kafala) to ensure their presence. This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on two key questions: how long can the surety be demanded, and does the defendant’s social standing affect this obligation? Understanding these positions is essential for correctly applying Hanafi qada (judicial procedure).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed issues
The passage addresses two separate but related questions: (1) the maximum duration for which a surety can be taken from a defendant, and (2) whether a defendant of high social standing (wajih) may be exempted from providing a surety altogether.
Keep these issues distinct in your analysis.
2
State each imam's position on the time limit
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a surety can be demanded for a maximum of three days. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it lasts only until the next court session. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani does not offer a separate view on duration in this passage; his view concerns the exemption.
3
State each imam's position on the wajih exemption
According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmitted corpus), there is no distinction: every defendant must provide a surety, whether wajih or not. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that a defendant of known standing and trustworthiness, who is unlikely to flee, should not be compelled to give a surety.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The author of al-Hidayah declares Abu Hanifa's three-day limit as correct and states that Zahir al-Riwayah makes no exception for wajih defendants. Therefore, the relied-upon position is a three-day surety for all defendants, without exemption.
This is the ruling followed in Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کفیل لینے کے سلسلہ میں تین دن کی تحدید حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی روایت ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے اور نہ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کی دوسری مجلس منعقد ہونے تک مدعی علیہ سے کفیل لیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق وجیہ اور غیر وجیہ آدمی کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے یعنی مدعی علیہ وجیہ ہو یا غیر وجیہہ آدمی اور مال دعوای حقیر ہو یا کثیر ہو بہر صورت مدعی علیہ کو فیل دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ حضرت امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ مدعی علیہ اگر زی و جاہت آدمی ہو اور ایسا معروف و مشہور ہو کہ بظاہر وہ اپنے آپ کو روپوش نہیں کرے گا تو ایسی صورت میں مدعلی علیہ کو فیل دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
The author of al-Hidayah says: Regarding the taking of a surety, the limit of three days is the narration of Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is correct. And Imam Abu Yusuf says that a surety will be taken from the defendant until the second session of the judge is held. The author of al-Hidayah said: According to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is no difference between a wajih (distinguished) and a non-wajih person, meaning whether the defendant is wajih or non-wajih, and whether the claimed property is insignificant or large, in any case the defendant will be compelled to give a surety. Imam Muhammad said: If the defendant is a person of standing and reputation, such that apparently he will not conceal himself, then in such a case the defendant will not be compelled to give a surety.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on two issues: the time limit for which a surety can be demanded, and whether a defendant's social standing (wajahah) exempts him from giving a surety. First, on the time limit: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a surety can be demanded for up to three days, meaning the plaintiff has three days to produce evidence. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the surety lasts only until the next court session (the second sitting). The author of al-Hidayah states that Abu Hanifa's view is correct (and this is the relied-upon position). Second, on social standing: According to the unambiguous narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah), there is no distinction: every defendant must provide a surety regardless of his status or the amount claimed. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the defendant is a person of high standing and reputation, well-known and unlikely to flee, then he is not compelled to give a surety. This opinion is not adopted as the mufta bihi (operative ruling); the school follows the general rule from Zahir al-Riwayah that all defendants must provide a surety if required.

Key Terms
وجیہ (wajih): A person of high social standing, reputation, and trustworthiness.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), how long can a surety be demanded from the defendant?
A) Until the next court session
B) For three days
C) No time limit
D) Until the case is decided

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a surety is required from all defendants for up to three days, regardless of social status, as per Zahir al-Riwayah.

Condition for Demanding Surety: Plaintiff Must Declare Witnesses Present
States a necessary condition for taking a surety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for demanding a surety in Hanafi fiqh and apply it to scenarios where the plaintiff’s witnesses are absent or nonexistent.

Core Idea
Without witnesses present, a surety serves no purpose in guaranteeing the defendant's attendance.

In a lawsuit, the plaintiff may require the defendant to provide a surety (kafil) to ensure his appearance in court. But is this right unconditional? According to al-Hidayah, the plaintiff must first declare that he has witnesses available in the city. This lesson examines the legal reasoning behind this condition and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act under discussion is the plaintiff's right to demand a surety (kafala) from the defendant in a court case.
This is not the contract of kafala itself, but a procedural right.
2
State the condition
The plaintiff must affirm that his witnesses are present in the city (shahr). If he says he has no witnesses or they are absent, the right to demand a surety is forfeited.
The condition is about the plaintiff’s declaration, not the actual existence of witnesses.
3
Understand the rationale
The benefit (fa'ida) of surety here is to ensure the defendant’s presence so that witnesses can testify. If no witnesses are available, the surety is meaningless.
This reasoning is based on istihsan (juristic preference).
4
Apply to scenarios
If the plaintiff claims witnesses are absent or nonexistent, the judge should not require a surety. Only when the plaintiff states witnesses are present may the judge order a surety.
The condition is a precondition for the validity of demanding a surety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ کفالہ کیلئے دی کا یہ کہنا ضروری ہے کہ میرے گواہ شہر میں موجود ہیں حتی کہ اگر ندی نے کہا کہ میرے پاس گواہ نہیں ہیں یا میرے گواہ غائب ہیں تو اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں کفیل لینے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ کفالہ کا فائدہ تو یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کے عاجز ہونے پر کفیل مدعی علیہ کو حاضر کز دے لیکن جب گواہ ہی موجود نہیں ہیں تو مد علی علیہ کو کیسے حاضر کیا جائے گا۔
The author of al-Hidayah said: For kafala, it is necessary for the plaintiff to say: 'My witnesses are present in the city.' Even if the plaintiff said: 'I have no witnesses' or 'My witnesses are absent,' then in that case a surety will not be taken from the defendant because in that case there is no benefit in taking a surety. The benefit of kafala is that when the witnesses are unable, the surety will produce the defendant. But when witnesses are not present, how will the defendant be produced?
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement. It establishes a condition for demanding a surety: the plaintiff must assert that he has witnesses present in the city. The legal reasoning is based on the purpose of kafala in this context. The surety is meant to ensure the defendant's availability so that the plaintiff can bring his witnesses to testify. If the plaintiff has no witnesses or they are absent, the surety serves no purpose because there is no evidence to present. Therefore, in such a case, a surety cannot be demanded. This ruling aligns with the earlier istihsan reasoning that the benefit of kafala is to enable the plaintiff to establish his case. Without witnesses, the benefit disappears.

Key Terms
شہر (shehr): The city or town where the court is located; the witnesses must be available locally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a surety be demanded from the defendant according to the author of al-Hidayah?
A) The plaintiff must have a written contract
B) The defendant must be a traveler
C) The plaintiff must state that his witnesses are present in the city
D) The claim must involve a large amount of money

Key Takeaway
The plaintiff must declare that his witnesses are in the city; otherwise, demanding a surety is pointless.

Plaintiff Accompanying Defendant and Exception for Travelers
Ruling with proof on plaintiff's accompaniment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for plaintiff accompanying a defendant and identify the exception for travelers, explaining the rationale of istihsan.

Core Idea
Accompaniment ensures the plaintiff's right, but hardship to a traveler limits it to the court session.

In Hanafi court procedure, when a defendant cannot provide a surety, the plaintiff may be ordered to accompany him like a shadow to prevent escape. However, this rule is not absolute: for travelers and foreigners, such accompaniment would cause undue hardship by delaying their journey. The school uses istihsan to limit the accompaniment to the duration of the judge's session, after which the court disposes of the case with an oath. This lesson unpacks the rule, its exception, and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
Locate the principal ruling: if the defendant does not produce a surety, the plaintiff is ordered to accompany him (daman-gir) at all times to secure his right.
This is the general Hanafi position for local defendants.
2
Identify the exception
Find the exception (illa an yakuna...) for travelers or foreigners. For them, accompaniment is only permitted until the end of the judge's court session.
The exception applies to both taking a surety and the accompaniment order.
3
Understand the rationale (istihsan)
Analyze why the exception exists: forcing a traveler to be accompanied beyond the session would cause harm (darar) by hindering his journey. Istihsan avoids this harm.
The proof is based on istihsan/maslaha, not a direct textual source.
4
Note the procedural outcome
If the plaintiff cannot present evidence by session's end, the judge administers an oath to the defendant and passes a verdict without waiting for evidence.
This balances the plaintiff's right against the defendant's convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر مدعلی علیہ نے اپنی طرف سے کفیل دید یا تو فبہا ورنہ مدعی کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مدعی علیہ کے ساتھ ساتھ اس کا دامن گیر رہے یعنی ہر وقت مدعی علیہ کے ساتھ لگا ر ہے تا کہ اس کا حق ضائع نہ ہو۔ ہاں اگر مدعلی علیہ پر دیس میں ہو یا مسافر ہو تو اس صورت میں مجلس قاضی کے ختم ہونے تک مدعی علیہ کے ساتھ ساتھ رہنے کی اجازت دی جائے گی پس جب قاضی کے عدالت سے اٹھنے کا وقت آ جائے اور مدعی بعینہ پیش نہ کر سکے تو قاضی مدنی علیہ سے قسم لے کر فیصلہ صادر کرے گا اور بینہ کے آنے کا انتظار نہ کرے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اسی طرح پر دیسی مدعی علیہ سے اگر کفیل لیا گیا تو صرف قاضی کی مجلس کے اختتام تک لیا جائے گا پس استثناء الا ان يكون الخ کفیل لینے اور مدنی علیہ کے ساتھ ساتھ رہے دونوں کی طرف راجع ہے کیونکہ قاضی کی نشست سے زیادہ کے اسطے کفیل لینا یا مد ٹی علیہ کے ساتھ ساتھ رہنے کی اجازت دینا پردیسی مسافر کے حق میں ایسا ضر ر ہے جو اس کو سفر سے روکتا ہے اور قاضی کی مجلس کے اختتام تک کفیل لینے یا ساتھ ساتھ رہنے میں بظاہر ایسا ضر ر نہیں ہے اور ساتھ ساتھ رہنے کی کیفیت کو کتاب الحجر میں ان شاء اللہ بیان کریں گے۔
The author of Quduri said: If the defendant gives a surety from his side, then well and good; otherwise, the plaintiff will be ordered to accompany the defendant and stick to him at all times so that his right is not lost. Yes, if the defendant is a foreigner or a traveler, then in that case he will be permitted to accompany him only until the end of the judge's session. Then when the time for the judge to leave the court comes and the plaintiff cannot present the evidence, the judge will administer an oath to the defendant and pass a verdict, and will not wait for the evidence to arrive. The author of al-Hidayah says: Similarly, if a surety is taken from a foreign defendant, it will only be taken until the end of the judge's session. So the exception (illa an yakuna...) refers to both taking a surety and allowing accompaniment, because taking a surety or allowing accompaniment for more than the judge's session is harmful to the foreign traveler as it prevents him from his journey. And for the duration of the judge's session, there is apparently no such harm. The manner of accompaniment will be explained in the Book of Hajar (detention) if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the scenario when no surety is given. The Hanafi school provides an alternative: the plaintiff may be ordered to accompany the defendant (like a shadow) to prevent his escape. This ensures the plaintiff's right is protected. However, this is not absolute. If the defendant is a stranger or traveler (from out of town), forcing him to be accompanied beyond the court session would cause hardship (darar) by delaying his journey. Therefore, in such cases, the accompaniment is limited to the duration of the judge's court session. After the session ends, if the plaintiff has not brought evidence, the judge administers an oath to the defendant and disposes of the case; he does not wait for evidence. The same principle applies to taking a surety from a traveler: the surety is only taken for the term of the court session. The author of al-Hidayah clarifies that the exception (for travelers) in the text refers both to taking a surety and to the accompaniment order. The rationale is avoiding harm to the traveler. This shows the Hanafi school's concern for balancing the plaintiff's right with the defendant's convenience.

Key Terms
دامن گیر (daman-gir): Literally 'skirt-holder'; a person who accompanies another constantly to prevent escape.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the defendant is a traveler and no surety is given?
A) The plaintiff accompanies him for three days
B) The defendant is immediately released
C) The plaintiff may accompany him only until the court session ends
D) The judge detains the defendant

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school orders plaintiff accompaniment to secure rights but limits it for travelers to prevent hardship, using istihsan.

Manner of Administering Oath and Its Emphasis
Begins a new chapter on oath procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that oaths must be taken by Allah alone, explain the concept of tawghlidh (solemn emphasis), and apply the judge's discretion in emphasizing oaths based on the character of the defendant.

Core Idea
An oath in court must be by Allah alone; emphasis (tawghlidh) using divine attributes is at the judge's discretion.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces the procedure for administering oaths in Islamic courts. The fundamental rule is that an oath must be sworn by Allah, not by any other being or object. The text provides prophetic evidence and explains how a judge may add solemn emphasis (tawghlidh) by citing Allah's attributes to deter perjury. It also touches on the judge's discretion and a reported view regarding not emphasizing on righteous individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
State that the oath must be taken by Allah alone, not by any other being or object.
This is the foundational principle from which all else follows.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the two hadiths quoted: one commanding oath by Allah or silence, and one warning against swearing by other than Allah as shirk.
The command in the hadith indicates obligation (wajib) per Hanafi usul.
3
Understand tawghlidh
Define tawghlidh as the solemn emphasis by mentioning Allah's attributes, and analyze the example formula given.
The attributes increase the weight of the oath to discourage falsehood.
4
Analyze judicial discretion
Explain that the judge may choose to emphasize or not, but must be cautious not to cause repetition of the oath.
Only one oath is due, so repetition would be invalid.
5
Examine the reported view
Note the view (qila) that a person known for righteousness should not be subjected to an emphasized oath.
This reflects consideration of the defendant's character.

فصل في كيفية اليمين والاستخلاف

ال دون الــ
ترجمہ قسم تو اللہ ہی کے نام سے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کے نام سے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے تم میں سے جو کوئی قسم کھائے تو وہ اللہ کے نام سے قسم کھائے یا اس کو چھوڑ دے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے اللہ تعالیٰ کے سواء کسی دوسرے کی قسم کھائی تو اس نے شرک کیا اور کبھی قسم کو اللہ کے ذکر کے اوصاف کے ساتھ مؤکد کیا جاتا ہے اور ذکر اوصاف زیادہ تختی کے لئے ہے جیسے اس کا قول کہ تو یوں کہہ اس ذات کی قسم جس کے سواء کوئی معبود نہیں ہے وہ حاضر غائب کا جاننے والا ہے وہی رحمن و رحیم ہے جو پوشیدہ اور باطن کو علانیہ اور ظاہر کے مانند جانتا ہے کہ فلاں شخص کا کوئی حق تجھ پر یا تیری جانب مال ہے جس کا مدعی نے دعوی کیا ہے اور وہ اتنا اور انتامال ہے نہیں ہے اور اس کو اس عبارت پر زیادہ کر کے تغلیط کرے اور اس کو اس عبارت سے کم کرنے کا بھی اختیار ہے مگر قاضی اس بات کی احتیاط رکھے کہ مدبلی علیہ پر قسم مکرر نہ ہو جائے کیونکہ مدعی علیہ پر صرف ایک قسم واجب ہے اور قاضی کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے تغلیظ کرے اور جی چاہے تو تغلیظ نہ کرے۔
Chapter: On the manner of the oath and administering the oath. Translation: A chapter on the description of the oath and taking the oath. He said: The oath is by Allah alone, not by other than Him, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' And sometimes the oath is emphasized by mentioning His attributes, and that is tawghlidh (solemn emphasis). For example, he says: 'Say: By Allah, besides Whom there is no god, the Knower of the unseen and the seen, the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate, Who knows the secret and the hidden as He knows the open, that so-and-so has no right against you, nor do you owe him this property which he claims, which is such-and-such, and nothing of it is owed.' And he may increase the emphasis in this wording, or decrease it, but he should be cautious lest the oath be repeated, because only one oath is due. The judge has the option: if he wishes, he may emphasize, and if he wishes, he may not emphasize. He says: 'Say: By Allah, or by Allah.' And it is said: He should not emphasize on a person known for righteousness, but emphasize on others. And it is said: [unclear]. Translation: The oath is taken in the name of Allah alone, not by other than Him, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' And sometimes the oath is emphasized by mentioning Allah's attributes, and that is for solemn emphasis. For example, he says: 'Say: By the Being besides Whom there is no god, the Knower of the unseen and the seen, the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate, Who knows the hidden and the secret as He knows the open, that so-and-so has no right against you, nor do you owe this property which the plaintiff claims, which is such-and-such, and nothing of it is owed.' And he may increase or decrease this wording, but the judge should be cautious lest the oath be repeated because only one oath is due. And the judge has the option: if he wishes, he may emphasize, and if he wishes, he may not emphasize.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new chapter (fasl) on the procedure for administering oaths. It is a ruling with proof from hadith. The key principle is that oaths must be taken in the name of Allah alone, citing two hadiths: one commanding oath by Allah or silence, and another warning that swearing by other than Allah is shirk. The judge may administer a solemn oath (tawghlidh) by including attributes of Allah (like 'Knower of the unseen and the seen', 'Most Compassionate') to make the oath more weighty and deter perjury. The text provides a formula for the emphasized oath. The judge may increase or decrease the number of attributes used, but must be careful not to make the defendant repeat the oath multiple times, as only one oath is due. The judge has discretion to use emphasis or not. There is also a reported view (qila) that a person known for righteousness should not be subjected to an emphasized oath, while others should. This reflects the Hanafi approach of considering the character of the defendant. The corrupted Arabic after 'qila' could not be read.

Key Terms
تغلیظ (tawghlidh): Solemn emphasis added to an oath by mentioning Allah's attributes to prompt truthfulness.
یمین (yamin): An oath; a solemn declaration by Allah used as evidence in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the rule that oaths must be taken by Allah alone?
A) Consensus of scholars
B) Qur'anic verse
C) Hadith of the Prophet
D) Reason and logic

Key Takeaway
Oaths in a Hanafi court must be by Allah alone; the judge may add emphasis using divine attributes at his discretion, and should be cautious not to repeat the oath.

Qada — Judiciary

The Oath is Only by Allah: Proof and Taghliz
Explaining the ruling on oath by Allah and the permissibility of taghliz by attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a valid oath is only by Allah, explain the proof from hadith, and identify the judge's discretion in applying taghliz (solemnification).

Core Idea
An oath by other than Allah is invalid and sinful; only an oath by Allah is legally binding.

In Islamic judicial procedure, the oath (yamin) is a crucial tool to determine truth when evidence is lacking. This lesson examines the foundational ruling that an oath must be by Allah alone, supported by explicit hadith. We also explore the concept of taghliz—emphasizing the oath by mentioning Allah's attributes—and the judge's discretionary power to tailor the oath to the defendant's character and the claim's value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn of Quduri states: 'The oath is by Allah to the exclusion of others.' Identify the act (oath) and its legal ruling: it is only valid when taken by Allah's name or attributes.
This is the core ruling of the chapter.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two hadith are cited. First: 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' Second: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' Confirm the sources: Bukhari/Muslim and Tirmidhi.
The second hadith indicates the prohibition and invalidity.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The imperative 'falyahlif' in the first hadith indicates obligation to swear by Allah specifically. The second hadith explicitly forbids swearing by other than Allah, using the strong term 'ashrak' (committed shirk), which implies the oath is not only invalid but also sinful.
This establishes the hukm: haram and batil.
4
Understand Taghliz
The author then explains that the oath may be emphasized by mentioning Allah's attributes (taghliz). This is not mandatory; it is a tool to deter false swearing. The judge may increase or decrease the attributes based on the defendant's character.
Taghliz is discretionary, not a requirement.
5
Note the Judge's Discretion
The judge has the option to apply taghliz or not. Two opinions are mentioned: some say it should not be applied to the righteous, others say it applies based on the value of the claim. The judge chooses based on the situation.
The mufta bihi is that the judge has full discretion.

تشریح مصنف جب قسم اور قسم کے مواقع سے فراغت پاچکے تو اب اس فصل میں قسم کی صفت اور کیفیت کو ذکر فرمائیں گے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ تم اللہ کے اسماء میں سے کسی اسم کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اور اللہ کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کے نام کے ساتھ قسم نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ بخاری اور مسلم کی ایک حدیث میں اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم میں سے اگر کوئی شخص قسم کھائے تو اللہ کی قسم کھائے یا اس کو چھوڑ دنے اور ایک حدیث میں او لیڈر کی جگہ اولیصمت ہے یعنی یا خاموش رہے اور ترندی کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے اللہ کے سواء کسی دوسرے کے نام سے قسم کھائی تو اس نے شرک کیا ان دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ قسم صرف اللہ کے نام کے ساتھ کھائی جاسکتی ہے اس کے سوا کسی دوسرے کے نام کے ساتھ قسم کھانا درست نہیں ہے اگر کھائی بھی گئی تو قسم منعقد نہ ہوگی ۔

صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ قسم کو اللہ کے اوصاف ذکر کر کے مؤکہ بھی کیا جاسکتا ہے اور ذکر اوصاف کے ساتھ قسم کو مؤگر تغلیظ ہوتا ہے یعنی قسم کو زیادہ سخت کرنا ہوتا ہے مثلا قاضی یہ الفاظ کہلائے والله الذى لا اله الا هو عالم الغيب والشهادة هو الرحمن الرحيم الذى يعلم من السر والخفاء ما يعلم من العلانية ما لغلا هذا عليك و لا قبلك هذا المال الذى أعاه وهو كذا وكذا ولا شيء منه اس ذات کی قسم جس کے سواء کوئی معبود نہیں وہ حاضر و غائب کا جاننے والا ہے وہی رحمن و رحیم ہے جو پوشیدہ اور باطن کو علانیہ اور ظاہر کی طرح جانتا ہے فلاں شخص کا تجھ پر یعنی مجھ پر یا میری جانب یعنی میری جانب اصل مال میں سے جس کا مدعی نے دعوی کیا ہے اور وہ اس قدر مال ہے نہیں ہے اور نہ اس میں سے کچھ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ تغلیظ کے سلسلہ میں قاضی مذکورہ الفاظ پر اضافہ بھی کر سکتا ہے اور ان میں سے کم بھی کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ قسم دلانے سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ قسم سے انکار کر دے تا کہ مدعی کا حق ثابت ہو جائے ۔ اور لوگوں کی حالتیں مختلف ہیں بعض لوگ ایسے نیک اور دیندار ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ صرف لفظ اللہ کے ساتھ قسم کھانے کی جسارت نہیں کرتے ۔ لہذا ایسے حضرات کے حق میں قسم کو غلیظ کرنے کے لئے لفظ اللہ کے علاوہ دوسرے اوصاف زیادہ کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور بعض لوگ ادنی درجہ کی تغلیظ سے قسم کھانے سے رک جاتے ہیں اور بعض ایسے بد دین اور نا نجار قسم کے لوگ ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ بغیر زیادتی تغلیظ کے باز نہیں آتے ۔ پس قاضی لوگوں کے حالات کی رعایت کر کے الفاظ قسم میں کمی ، زیادتی کرنے کا مجاز ہے اس زیادتی کے سلسلہ میں ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث اصل ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ ایک شخص نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے قسم کھائی اور یہ کہا والله الذى لا اله الاهو الرحمن الرحيم الذي انزل علیک الکتاب - اس ذات کی قسم جس کے سواء کوئی معبود نہیں ہے وہی رحمن و رحیم ہے اسی نے تجھ پر کتاب اتاری ہے یہ سن کر اللہ کے رسول نے کوئی نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ لہذا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ الفاظ تم میں تغلیظ کے لئے زیادتی کی اجازت ہے لیکن الفاظ قسم زیادہ کراتے وقت قاضی بہت ؟ و محتاط رہے یعنی اللہ کے اسماء اور صفات کو بغیر واؤ کے ذکر کرنے کی ہدایت کرے کیونکہ اگر مدعی علیہ نے واللہ والرحمن والرحیم واؤ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا تو تین قسمیں ہو جائیں گی۔ حالانکہ اس پر واجب ایک ہی قسم ہے بہر حال قاضی کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے تغلیظ کرے اور الفاظ قسم زیادہ
The author (Quduri) said: If the defendant gives a guarantor from his side, then fine, otherwise the plaintiff will be ordered to accompany the defendant and seize his garment, i.e., stay attached to the defendant at all times so that his right is not lost. Yes, if the defendant is a foreigner or traveler, then in that case permission to accompany the defendant will be given until the end of the court session. Then when the time comes for the judge to leave the court and the plaintiff cannot produce the defendant in person, the judge will take an oath from the defendant and issue a verdict, and will not wait for the evidence to arrive. The author of Hidayah says: Similarly, if a guarantor is taken from a foreign defendant, it will be taken only until the end of the judge's session. So the exception (except if...) applies to both taking a guarantor and accompanying the defendant, because taking a guarantor for longer than the judge's sitting or allowing accompaniment of the defendant for the traveler is a harm that prevents him from traveling, and taking a guarantor or accompanying until the end of the judge's session apparently does not cause such harm. The manner of accompaniment will be explained in the Book of Hajar, God willing. Chapter on the Manner of the Oath and Administering the Oath. Translation: Chapter on the manner of the oath and administering the oath. Statement of the manner of the oath. He said: The oath is by Allah to the exclusion of others, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever among you swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' And sometimes it is emphasized by mentioning His attributes, and that is taghliz (solemnification). An example is when he says: 'Say: By Allah, besides whom there is no god, the Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, who knows of secret and hidden what He knows of what is public. Such and such a person has no right upon you nor from you this property which he claims, and it is such and such, and none of it is yours.' And he may increase in taghliz beyond this, and he may decrease from it, except that he should be careful so that the oath is not repeated upon him, because the obliged person has only one oath. And the judge has the option: if he wishes, he may make it solemn, and if he wishes, he may not. So he says: 'Say: By Allah' or 'By Allah.' And it was said that he should not make it solemn for one known for righteousness, but should make it solemn for others. And it was said that he should make it solemn for significant wealth and not for insignificant wealth. Commentary: When the author has finished discussing the oath and its occasions, he now mentions in this chapter the description and manner of the oath. So he says: The oath occurs with one of the names of Allah, and does not occur with the name of other than Allah, because in a hadith in Bukhari and Muslim, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If any of you swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' And in another hadith, instead of 'aw liyadhar' it is 'aw liyasmut' meaning 'or remain silent.' And in Tirmidhi's hadith: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' From these two hadiths it is understood that the oath can only be taken by the name of Allah; swearing by the name of other than Allah is not permissible, and if done, the oath is not valid. Al-Quduri said that the oath can be emphasized by mentioning Allah's attributes, and mentioning the attributes makes the oath more solemn, i.e., makes the oath more severe. For example, the judge makes him say: 'By Allah, besides whom there is no god, the Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, who knows of secret and hidden as He knows what is public. Such and such a person has no right upon you nor from you this property which he claims, and it is such and such, and none of it is yours.' The author of Hidayah says: In the matter of taghliz, the judge may increase upon the mentioned words and may decrease from them, because the purpose of administering the oath is that the defendant should refuse the oath so that the plaintiff's right is established. And people's conditions differ: some people are so righteous and religious that they do not dare to swear even by the word 'Allah' alone. Therefore, for such persons there is no need to add other attributes to make the oath solemn. Some people are deterred from swearing by the lowest degree of solemnity, and some are so evil and dishonest that they do not refrain without increased solemnity. So the judge, observing people's conditions, is authorized to decrease or increase the words of the oath. In this regard, the hadith of Abu Hurairah is the basis. It is narrated that a man swore in the presence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'By Allah, besides whom there is no god, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, who sent down to you the Book.' Hearing this, the Messenger of Allah did not disapprove. Thus it is understood that increase in words for taghliz is permitted. However, when making the words of the oath more, the judge should be very [?] careful, i.e., he should instruct to mention the names and attributes of Allah without the 'and', because if the defendant says 'By Allah, and by the Most Gracious, and by the Most Merciful' with the 'and', then three oaths would occur, whereas only one oath is obligatory upon him. In any case, the judge has the option: if he wishes, he may make it solemn and increase the words of the oath.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa), specifically the chapter on the manner of the oath (yamin) and its administration (istihlaf). The text begins with the matn of Quduri, stating that the oath is only by Allah, to the exclusion of any other entity. The proof comes from two hadith: (1) The Prophet (SAW) said, 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' (2) 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' These hadith establish that swearing by other than Allah is not only invalid but also sinful. The passage then introduces the concept of taghliz (solemnification), where the judge can emphasize the oath by mentioning the attributes of Allah, such as His omniscience and mercy. The purpose is to make the oath more awe-inspiring so that a dishonest defendant hesitates to swear falsely. The judge has discretion to increase or decrease the attributes based on the defendant's character: a pious person may be deterred by a simple oath, while a wicked person may need a more solemn form. However, the judge must be cautious not to cause multiple oaths accidentally; for example, if the defendant repeats 'By Allah, and by the Most Gracious, and by the Most Merciful' with the conjunction 'waw', that would count as three separate oaths, whereas only one is required. The author of Hidayah adds that the underlying principle is to establish the plaintiff's right; the oath is a means to that end. Thus the judge tailors the administration of the oath to the situation.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath taken by the defendant in court, affirming the truth of his denial of the claim.
التغليظ (al-taghliz): Solemnification of the oath by adding attributes of Allah to make it more awe-inspiring and deter false swearing.
الاستخلاف (al-istihlaf): The judge administering the oath to the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, which of the following is true about swearing an oath in court?
A) The oath can be taken by any sacred entity (e.g., the Quran, the Prophet).
B) The oath is only by Allah, and swearing by other than Allah is invalid and sinful.
C) The judge must always administer the most solemn form of oath with all attributes.
D) The defendant can choose to swear by any name of God he wishes.

Key Takeaway
The valid oath in a Hanafi court is only by Allah; swearing by anything else is invalid and sinful, and the judge has discretion to emphasize the oath based on the defendant and the case.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Validity and Intensification of Oaths in Hanafi Law
Ruling on oath being by Allah and its intensification with attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of oaths by other than Allah, and apply the qadi's discretion in intensifying an oath based on the defendant's character and the value of the claim.

Core Idea
An oath is valid only by Allah's name or attributes; swearing by other than Allah is invalid.

In legal proceedings, the manner of taking an oath can determine whether justice is served. This lesson from Al-Hidayah explains that only oaths by Allah are recognized, and that the qadi may intensify the oath by invoking divine attributes to deter falsehood. Understanding these rules enables you to apply the correct procedure in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine that the act being ruled is swearing an oath. The ruling is that it must be by Allah or His attributes; swearing by other than Allah is invalid.
The passage explicitly states that if sworn by other than Allah, the oath does not take effect (ghayr mun'aqid).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadiths cited: Bukhari/Muslim: 'Whoever swears an oath, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' Tirmidhi: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.'
These are ahadith (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning is definitive (qat'i al-dalala) on this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyahlif' indicates obligation to swear by Allah. The prohibition 'fad ashraka' shows that swearing by other is invalid (shirk).
The imperative (amr) in Hanafi usul indicates wujub unless overridden.
4
Note the scope of taghliz
The passage introduces intensification (taghliz) as a permissible addition. The qadi may add attributes like 'al-Rahman, al-Rahim' etc. to stress the oath.
Supported by hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet did not object to an intensified oath.
5
Examine the qadi's discretion
The qadi has discretion to add or reduce words based on the defendant's character (pious vs. wicked) and the value of the claim. Two opinions exist: one considers piety, the other claim value.
The purpose of intensification is to deter falsehood; the qadi balances that purpose with not overburdening the pious.

کیونکہ اگر مدعی علیہ نے واللہ والرحمن والرحیم واؤ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا تو تین قسمیں ہو جائیں گی۔ حالانکہ اس پر واجب ایک ہی قسم ہے بہر حال قاضی کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے تغلیظ کرے اور الفاظ قسم زیادہ کرنے کی ہدایت کرے اور جی چاہے تو تغلیظ نہ کرے اور صرف بالہ یا اللہ کہلانے پر اکتفاء کرے بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ اگر مدعی علیہ، صلاح اور تقویٰ کے ساتھ معروف اور مشہور ہو تو اس پر تغلیظ نہ کرے اور دوسروں پر تغلیظ کرے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ اگر مال دعوی کثیر ہو تو قسم میں تغلیظ کرے اور اگر مال دعوی حقیر ہو تو تغلیظ نہ کرے۔
Explanation of the author: When he has finished discussing the oath and its occasions, now in this chapter he will mention the attribute and quality of the oath. Thus he said: The oath is with one of the names of Allah, and the oath is not with the name of anyone other than Allah, because in a hadith of Bukhari and Muslim, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever among you swears an oath, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' And in one hadith, instead of 'aw liyadhar' it is 'aw liyasmut', meaning keep silent. And in Tirmidhi's hadith: 'Whoever swears by other than Allah has committed shirk.' From these two hadiths it is understood that an oath can only be taken by the name of Allah; swearing by anyone else is not correct, and if taken, the oath will not be contracted. Sahib Quduri said that an oath can be made stressed (mu'akkad) by mentioning the attributes of Allah, and mentioning the attributes makes the oath intensified (taghliz), meaning it makes the oath more severe. For example, the qadi should make him say: 'By Allah, there is no god but Him, the Knower of the unseen and the seen, He is the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate, who knows the secret and the hidden as He knows the open. Nothing of this property which he claims is due to you from me, nor anything of it.' The author of al-Hidayah says: Regarding taghliz, the qadi can add to these words or reduce from them, because the purpose of making him swear is that the defendant should refuse the oath so that the plaintiff's right is established. And people's conditions differ; some are so pious and religious that they do not dare to swear even by just the word 'Allah', so there is no need to add other attributes for intensification in their case. Some people stop from swearing with a lower degree of intensification, and some are so evil and wicked that they do not desist without greater intensification. So the qadi, taking into account the conditions of the people, is permitted to increase or decrease the words of the oath. In this matter of increase, the hadith of Abu Hurairah is the basis. It is narrated that a man swore in the presence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'By Allah, there is no god but Him, the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate, who sent down the Book to you.' Hearing this, the Messenger of Allah did not disapprove. Thus it is understood that addition of words for taghliz is permitted. However, when making the words of the oath longer, the qadi should be very careful, i.e., he should instruct to mention the names and attributes of Allah without the conjunction 'waw', because if the defendant says 'by Allah, by the Most Merciful, by the Most Compassionate' with 'waw', then there will be three oaths, whereas only one oath is obligatory upon him. In any case, the qadi has discretion: if he wishes, he may intensify and instruct to increase the words of the oath; if he wishes, he may not intensify and suffice with just saying 'billah' or 'Allah'. Some scholars said that if the defendant is known for righteousness and piety, then do not intensify, and for others intensify. Some said that if the claimed property is substantial, then intensify, and if the claimed property is trivial, then do not intensify.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the manner of oath in legal proceedings. It opens by stating that an oath is valid only by one of Allah's names, supported by hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and Tirmidhi. The hadith 'man kana halifan falyahlif billah aw liyadhar' is cited, with a variant 'aw liyasmut'. Swearing by other than Allah is shirk and the oath does not take effect. Then the author (Sahib Quduri) adds that the oath can be made stressed by mentioning Allah's attributes, giving an example of a lengthy formula that the qadi can use to intensify the oath. The commentator (Sahib al-Hidayah) explains that the qadi has discretion to add or reduce the words based on the defendant's character: the pious need less, the wicked need more. This is supported by a hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet did not object to an intensified oath. A caution is given: attributes should be mentioned without the conjunction 'waw' to avoid multiple oaths. Finally, two opinions are cited: intensify based on the defendant's piety or based on the value of the claim. The passage emphasizes the qadi's role in balancing effectiveness and justice.

Key Terms
قسم (qasam): An oath; a formal declaration invoking Allah to confirm the truth of a statement in legal proceedings.
تغلیظ (taghliz): Intensification of an oath by adding emphasis through mentioning Allah's attributes, making the oath more solemn and deterrent.
مؤکہ (mu'akkadah): Emphasized or stressed; the oath strengthened by adding divine attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone swears by other than Allah?
A) The oath is valid but disliked.
B) The oath is invalid (does not take effect).
C) The oath is valid if the person is Muslim.
D) The oath becomes a binding promise.

Key Takeaway
An oath is valid only when sworn by Allah or His attributes; the qadi may intensify it by adding attributes, but this is discretionary.

Oath by Divorce or Emancipation: Prohibition and Exception
Primary ruling and exceptional permission for divorce/emancipation oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi ruling on administering oaths by divorce or emancipation, identify the hadith proof, and explain the exceptional permission for contentious defendants.

Core Idea
An oath by divorce is not permitted unless the defendant is contentious; necessity overrides the literal hadith.

This lesson examines a critical tension in Hanafi qada: the general prohibition of oaths by divorce or emancipation based on the Prophet's command to swear only by Allah, and the exceptional permission granted when the defendant is quarrelsome and disregards oaths by Allah. Understanding this balance between textual evidence and practical necessity is essential for judges and muftis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the qadi administering an oath phrased as a conditional divorce or emancipation. The default ruling is that it is not permitted (haram).
The text says 'ولا يستحلف بالطلاق والعتاق'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith narrated earlier: 'He who swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' This hadith restricts valid oaths to Allah alone.
Hadith from Sunan al-Nasa'i.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليحلف' indicates obligation, and 'بالله' specifies the only permissible object of the oath. The alternative 'أو ليذر' commands silence, implying any oath not by Allah is prohibited.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the exception and its condition
Some later scholars permitted the qadi to administer such an oath if the defendant is contentious and does not fear Allah. The condition is the defendant's quarrelsome nature.
Exception is based on istihsan for practical deterrent effect.
5
Evaluate the tension between the hadith and the exception
The commentary explicitly states the exception contradicts the hadith text but is accepted due to necessity. This illustrates how later fatwa may override literal proof when the objective of justice is at stake.
The exception carries authority of fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلاق اور عتاق کی قسم نہیں لی جائے گی
قال ولا يستحلف بالطلاق والعتاق لما روينا وقيل في زماننا اذا الحَ الخصم ساغ للقاضى ان يحلف بذالك لقلة المبالاة باليمين بالله وكثرة الامتناع بسبب الحلف بالطلاق
ترجمہ اور طلاق اور عتاق کی قسم نہ لی جائے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے، اور کہا گیا کہ ہمارے زمانے میں اگر مدعی علیہ نے زیادہ مبالغہ کیا تو قاضی کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اس کی قسم دلائے کیونکہ اللہ کی قسم کی پر واہ کم ہے اور حلف بالطلاق سے زیادہ برکتے ہیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ مدنی علیہ سے طلاق یا عقاق کی قسم نہیں کی جائے گی یعنی مدنی علیہ یہ نہ کہے گا کہ اگر مدعی کا دعوی صحیح ہوتو میری بیوی پر طلاق یا میرا غلام آزاد اور دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو شروع فصل میں گذر چکی ہے یعنی من كان حالفا فليحلف بالله او ليذر بعض مشائخ نے کہا نکه اگر مدعی علیہ جھگڑالو محسوس ہوتو قاضی اس سے طلاق یا عتاق کی قسم لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں اکثر لوگ فسق کی وجہ سے اللہ سے کم ڈرتے ہیں اور طلاق وغیرہ پڑ جانے سے گھبرا کر جھوٹی قسم کھانے سے رک جاتے ہیں پس جب قاضی محسوس کرے کہ مدعی علیہ جھگڑالو یا بے باک آدمی ہے تو اس سے طلاق یا عتاق کی قسم لے سکتا ہے یہ واضح رہے کہ یہ تم اگر چہ مفید ہے۔ لیکن نص حديث من كان حالفا فليحلف بالله اولیذر کے مخالف ہے۔
Oath by divorce and emancipation will not be taken. He said: And one should not administer an oath by divorce or emancipation due to what we narrated, and it was said: In our time, if the opponent is contentious, it is permissible for the qadi to administer an oath by that due to the lack of regard for the oath by Allah and the greater deterrence caused by the oath by divorce. Translation: And an oath by divorce and emancipation should not be taken due to the hadith we narrated. And it was said: In our time, if the defendant is very contentious, it is permissible for the qadi to administer an oath by that because care for the oath by Allah is less and they refrain more due to the oath by divorce. Commentary: The issue: An oath by divorce or emancipation should not be taken from the defendant, i.e., the defendant should not say 'If the plaintiff's claim is true, then my wife is divorced or my slave is free.' The proof is the hadith mentioned at the beginning of the chapter: 'He who swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.' Some scholars said that if the defendant is perceived as quarrelsome, the qadi can take an oath from him by divorce or emancipation because in that case most people, due to disobedience, fear Allah less and refrain from swearing falsely due to fear of divorce occurring. So when the qadi perceives that the defendant is quarrelsome or reckless, he can take an oath by divorce or emancipation. It should be clear that this opinion, although beneficial, is contrary to the text of the hadith 'He who swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent.'
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding oaths administered in court. The primary ruling, attributed to Imam al-Quduri, is that the qadi should not administer an oath by divorce (talaq) or emancipation (itaq). The evidence is the Prophet's hadith: 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.' This hadith, which appears earlier in the text, establishes that valid oaths are only by Allah. However, the author then introduces an exceptional view from later scholars: when the defendant is known to be quarrelsome and does not fear Allah, the qadi may use an oath by divorce or emancipation because the fear of losing family or property is a stronger deterrent. The commentary explains that this exception is contrary to the explicit wording of the hadith, but it is permitted as a practical necessity in corrupt times.

Key Terms
حلف بالطلاق (halfu bil-talaq): An oath phrased as a conditional divorce: e.g., 'If my claim is false, my wife is divorced.'
تغلیظ (taghlith): Emphasis in the oath, such as by specifying a particular attribute of Allah or using divorce/emancipation to deter perjury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for not administering an oath by divorce or emancipation?
A) The Quranic verse 'And do not make Allah an obstacle to your oaths'
B) The hadith 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or keep silent'
C) The practice of the Caliphs
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The default is prohibition; the exception is a necessity-based istihsan for quarrelsome defendants.
